<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg/220px-Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg/330px-Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg/440px-Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1596" data-file-height="1100" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dywizjon_303_in_color.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pilots of the <a href="/wiki/No._303_Polish_Fighter_Squadron" title="No. 303 Polish Fighter Squadron">303 <i>"Kościuszko"</i> Polish Fighter Squadron</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>, October 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the war, Poland made the fourth-largest troop contribution to <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">the Allied</a> war effort, after the Soviets, the British, and the Americans.<sup class="reference" id="ref_bnone"><a href="#endnote_bnone">[b]</a></sup> Polish troops fought under the command of both the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Government_in_Exile" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Government in Exile">Polish Government in Exile</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces_in_the_West" title="Polish Armed Forces in the West">west</a> and under Soviet leadership in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces_in_the_East" title="Polish Armed Forces in the East">east</a>. The Polish expeditionary corps, which was controlled by the exiled pre-war government based in London, played an important role in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">North African Campaigns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tobruk_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobruk-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-including_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-including-58">[58]</a></sup> They are particularly well remembered for their conduct at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Cassino" title="Battle of Monte Cassino">Battle of Monte Cassino</a>, a conflict which culminated in the raising of a Polish flag over the ruins of the mountain-top abbey by the <a href="/wiki/II_Corps_(Poland)" title="II Corps (Poland)">12th Podolian Uhlans</a>. The Polish forces in the west were commanded by Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Anders" title="Władysław Anders">Władysław Anders</a>, who had received his command from <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland" title="Prime Minister of Poland">prime minister</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile" title="Polish government-in-exile">exiled government</a> <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Sikorski" title="Władysław Sikorski">Władysław Sikorski</a>. In the east, the Soviet-backed <a href="/wiki/First_Polish_Army_(1944-1945)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Polish Army (1944-1945)">Polish 1st Army</a> distinguished itself in the battles for <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">Berlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-google4_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google4-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Polish servicemen were also active in the theatres of naval and air warfare; during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a> Polish squadrons such as the <a href="/wiki/No._303_Polish_Fighter_Squadron" title="No. 303 Polish Fighter Squadron">No. 303 "Kościuszko" fighter squadron</a><sup id="cite_ref-Olson_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-60">[60]</a></sup> achieved considerable success, and by the end of the war the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Air_Forces_in_France_and_Great_Britain" title="Polish Air Forces in France and Great Britain">exiled Polish Air Forces</a> could claim 769 confirmed kills. Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Navy" title="Polish Navy">Polish Navy</a> was active in the protection of convoys in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and Atlantic Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-PN_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PN-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg/170px-Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg/255px-Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg/340px-Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="875" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polish_Soldier%27s_Grave_Warsaw_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Grave of a <a href="/wiki/Polish_resistance_movement_in_World_War_II" title="Polish resistance movement in World War II">Polish <i>Home Army</i> resistance fighter</a> killed during the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a>. The battle lasted 63 days and resulted in the deaths of 200,000 civilians, 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the organised units of the 1st Army and the Forces in the Nazi-occupied Europe, the domestic underground resistance movement, the <a href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" class="mw-redirect" title="Armia Krajowa">Armia Krajowa</a> (<i>Home Army</i>), fought against the German occupation. The <a href="/wiki/Polish_resistance_movement_in_World_War_II" title="Polish resistance movement in World War II">wartime resistance movement</a> in Poland was one of the three largest resistance movements of the entire war,<sup class="reference" id="ref_cnone"><a href="#endnote_cnone">[c]</a></sup> and encompassed an unusually broad range of clandestine activities, which essentially functioned as an <a href="/wiki/Polish_Underground_State" title="Polish Underground State">underground state</a> complete with <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Poland_during_World_War_II" title="Education in Poland during World War II">degree-awarding universities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Special_Courts" title="Special Courts">a court system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salm42_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salm42-62">[62]</a></sup> The resistance was, however, largely loyal to the exiled government and generally resented the idea of a communist Poland; for this reason, in the summer of 1944 they initiated <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tempest" title="Operation Tempest">Operation Tempest</a>, of which the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a> that begun on 1 August 1944 was the best known operation.<sup id="cite_ref-Soviets_and_AK_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soviets_and_AK-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lerski1996-2_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lerski1996-2-64">[64]</a></sup> The objective of the uprising was to drive the German occupiers from the city and help with the larger fight against Germany and the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>. However, secondary motives for the uprising sought to see Warsaw liberated before the Soviets could reach the capital, so as to underscore Polish sovereignty by empowering the Polish Underground State before the Soviet-backed <a href="/wiki/Polish_Committee_of_National_Liberation" title="Polish Committee of National Liberation">Polish Committee of National Liberation</a> could assume control. However, a lack of available allied military aid and Stalin's reluctance to allow the 1st Army to help their fellow countrymen take the city, led to the uprising's failure and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Planned_destruction_of_Warsaw" title="Planned destruction of Warsaw">planned destruction of the city</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG/220px-WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG/330px-WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG/440px-WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG 2x" data-file-width="2007" data-file-height="2161" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_occupied_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="The Holocaust in occupied Poland">the Holocaust in occupied Poland</a> with deportation routes and massacre sites. Major <a href="/wiki/Jewish_ghettos_in_German-occupied_Poland" title="Jewish ghettos in German-occupied Poland">ghettos</a> marked with <a href="/wiki/Yellow_badge#Nazi_Europe" title="Yellow badge">yellow stars</a>. Germany's Nazi <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camps" class="mw-redirect" title="Extermination camps">extermination camps</a> marked with white skulls in black squares. The border in 1941 between Nazi Germany and the Soviet Union marked in red</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the war, German forces under direct order from <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> set up six major <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>, all of which operated in the heart of Poland. They included the notorious <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Majdanek_concentration_camp" title="Majdanek concentration camp">Majdanek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz</a> killing centers. This allowed the Germans to <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_train" title="Holocaust train">transport the condemned Jews</a> under the guise of resettlement from the Third Reich and across occupied Europe, and systematically murder them in the death camps set up in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_areas_annexed_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany">Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany</a>.</p>
<p>The Nazi crimes against the Polish nation claimed the lives of 2.9 million Polish Jews,<sup id="cite_ref-Materski.2FSzarota-2_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Materski.2FSzarota-2-65">[65]</a></sup> and 2.8 million ethnic Poles,<sup id="cite_ref-Materski.2FSzarota_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Materski.2FSzarota-66">[66]</a></sup> including Polish academics, doctors, lawyers, nobility, priests and numerous others. Since 3.5 million Jews lived in pre-war Poland, Jewish victims make up the largest percentage of all victims of the Nazis' extermination program. It is estimated that, of pre-war Poland's Jewry, approximately 90% were killed. Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–1945)">occupation</a>, many members of the Armia Krajowa, supported by the <a href="/wiki/Polish_government_in_exile" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish government in exile">Polish government in exile</a>, and millions of ordinary Poles – at great risk to themselves and their families – <a href="/wiki/Rescue_of_Jews_by_Poles_during_the_Holocaust" title="Rescue of Jews by Poles during the Holocaust">engaged in rescuing Jews from the Nazi Germans</a>. Grouped by nationality, Poles represent the largest number of people who rescued Jews during the Holocaust. To date, 6,620 Poles have been awarded the title of <i><a href="/wiki/Polish_Righteous_Among_the_Nations" title="Polish Righteous Among the Nations">Righteous Among the Nations</a></i> by the State of Israel–more than any other nation.<sup id="cite_ref-YV_Stats_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YV_Stats-67">[67]</a></sup> Some estimates put the number of Poles involved in rescue efforts at up to 3 million, and credit Poles with sheltering up to 450,000 Jews.</p>
<p>Also, some 150,000 Polish civilians were killed by Soviet Communists between 1939 and 1941 during the Soviet Union's occupation of eastern Poland (<a href="/wiki/Kresy" title="Kresy">Kresy</a>), and another estimated 100,000 Poles were killed by the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army" title="Ukrainian Insurgent Army">Ukrainian Insurgent Army</a> (UPA) in the regions of <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">Wołyń</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Eastern Galicia</a> between 1943 and 1944 in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Massacres_of_Poles_in_Volhynia_and_Eastern_Galicia" title="Massacres of Poles in Volhynia and Eastern Galicia">Wołyń Massacres</a>. The massacres were part of a vicious <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_clensing" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic clensing">ethnic clensing</a> campaign waged by Ukrainian nationalists against the local Polish population in the German-occupied territories of eastern Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the war's conclusion in 1945, Poland's borders <a href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland_immediately_after_World_War_II" title="Territorial changes of Poland immediately after World War II">were shifted westwards</a>, resulting in considerable territorial losses. Most of the Polish inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Kresy" title="Kresy">Kresy</a> <a href="/wiki/Polish_population_transfers_(1944%E2%80%9346)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish population transfers (1944–46)">were expelled</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Curzon_Line" title="Curzon Line">Curzon Line</a> in accordance with Stalin's agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-Lisocka-Jaegermann_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lisocka-Jaegermann-70">[70]</a></sup> The western border was moved to the <a href="/wiki/Oder-Neisse_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Oder-Neisse line">Oder-Neisse line</a>. As a result, Poland's territory was reduced by 20%, or 77,500 square kilometres (29,900&#160;sq&#160;mi). The shift forced the migration of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_evacuation_and_expulsion" title="World War II evacuation and expulsion">millions of other people</a>, most of whom were Poles, Germans, Ukrainians, and Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc5_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc5-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">Of all the countries involved</a> in the war, Poland <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–1945)">lost the highest percentage of its citizens</a>: over 6 million perished – nearly one-fifth of Poland's population – <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust in Poland">half of them</a> Polish Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-posterum0_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-posterum0-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-szma_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szma-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5MillionForgotten0_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5MillionForgotten0-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-expatica_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expatica-73">[73]</a></sup> Over 90% of deaths were non-military in nature. Population numbers did not recover until the 1970s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_communism">Post-war communism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_(1945%E2%80%931989)" title="History of Poland (1945–1989)">History of Poland (1945–1989)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic" title="Polish People's Republic">Polish People's Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Solidarity" title="History of Solidarity">History of Solidarity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polish_Round_Table_Agreement" title="Polish Round Table Agreement">Polish Round Table Agreement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg/170px-Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg" width="170" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg/255px-Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9e/Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="446" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>At <a href="/wiki/High_Noon" title="High Noon">High Noon</a>, 4 June 1989</i> – political poster featuring <a href="/wiki/Gary_Cooper" title="Gary Cooper">Gary Cooper</a> to encourage votes for the <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity</a> party in the <a href="/wiki/Contract_Sejm" title="Contract Sejm">1989 elections</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the insistence of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> sanctioned the formation of a new provisional pro-Communist coalition government in Moscow, which ignored the <a href="/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile" title="Polish government-in-exile">Polish government-in-exile</a> based in London; a move which angered many Poles who considered it a <a href="/wiki/Yalta_betrayal" class="mw-redirect" title="Yalta betrayal">betrayal</a> by the Allies. In 1944, Stalin had made guarantees to <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Churchill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Roosevelt</a> that he would maintain Poland's sovereignty and allow democratic elections to take place. However, upon achieving victory in 1945, the elections organized by the occupying Soviet authorities were falsified and were used to provide a veneer of 'legitimacy' for Soviet hegemony over Polish affairs. The Soviet Union instituted a new <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist</a> government in Poland, analogous to much of the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anti-Communism_in_the_Communist_Bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Communism in the Communist Bloc">As elsewhere in Communist Europe</a> the Soviet occupation of Poland met with <a href="/wiki/Cursed_soldiers" title="Cursed soldiers">armed resistance</a> from the outset which continued into the fifties.</p>
<p>Despite widespread objections, the new Polish government accepted the Soviet annexation of the pre-war eastern regions of Poland<sup id="cite_ref-indianapolis_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indianapolis-74">[74]</a></sup> (in particular the cities of <a href="/wiki/Wilno" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilno">Wilno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Lwów">Lwów</a>) and agreed to the permanent garrisoning of <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> units on Poland's territory. Military alignment within the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> throughout the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> came about as a direct result of this change in Poland's political culture and in the European scene came to characterise the full-fledged integration of Poland into the brotherhood of communist nations.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of Poland">People's Republic of Poland</a> (<i>Polska Rzeczpospolita Ludowa</i>) <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of the People's Republic of Poland">was officially proclaimed in 1952</a>. In 1956 after the death of <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_Bierut" title="Bolesław Bierut">Bolesław Bierut</a>, the régime of <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Gomu%C5%82ka" title="Władysław Gomułka">Władysław Gomułka</a> became temporarily more liberal, freeing many people from prison and expanding some personal freedoms. <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Polish_People%27s_Republic" title="Collectivization in the Polish People's Republic">Collectivization in the Polish People's Republic</a> failed. A similar situation repeated itself in the 1970s under <a href="/wiki/Edward_Gierek" title="Edward Gierek">Edward Gierek</a>, but most of the time persecution of <a href="/wiki/Anti-communist_resistance_in_Poland" title="Anti-communist resistance in Poland">anti-communist opposition</a> groups persisted. Despite this, Poland was at the time considered to be one of the least oppressive states of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Bloc">Soviet Bloc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PWN_historia_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PWN_historia-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Labour turmoil in 1980 led to the formation of the independent trade union "<a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity</a>" ("<i>Solidarność</i>"), which over time became a political force. Despite persecution and imposition of <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Poland" title="Martial law in Poland">martial law in 1981</a>, it eroded the dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_United_Workers%27_Party" title="Polish United Workers' Party">Polish United Workers' Party</a> and by 1989 had triumphed in Poland's first <a href="/wiki/Contract_Sejm" title="Contract Sejm">partially free and democratic parliamentary elections</a> since the end of the Second World War. <a href="/wiki/Lech_Wa%C5%82%C4%99sa" title="Lech Wałęsa">Lech Wałęsa</a>, a Solidarity candidate, eventually <a href="/wiki/Polish_presidential_election,_1990" title="Polish presidential election, 1990">won the presidency in 1990</a>. The Solidarity movement heralded the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">collapse of communist regimes and parties across Europe</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Present-day">Present-day</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_(1989%E2%80%93present)" title="History of Poland (1989–present)">History of Poland (1989–present)</a> and <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">2004 enlargement of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_and_PL_flags.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/EU_and_PL_flags.jpg/220px-EU_and_PL_flags.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/EU_and_PL_flags.jpg/330px-EU_and_PL_flags.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/EU_and_PL_flags.jpg/440px-EU_and_PL_flags.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="340" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_and_PL_flags.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flags of Poland and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>—the country became a member of the European community of nations on 1 May 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Shock_therapy_(economics)" title="Shock therapy (economics)">shock therapy</a> programme, initiated by <a href="/wiki/Leszek_Balcerowicz" title="Leszek Balcerowicz">Leszek Balcerowicz</a> in the early 1990s enabled the country to transform its socialist-style planned economy into a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. As with other post-communist countries, Poland suffered slumps in social and economic standards,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> but it became the first post-communist country to reach its pre-1989 GDP levels, which it achieved by 1995 largely thanks to its booming economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Real_GDP_growth_in_CEECs_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_GDP_growth_in_CEECs-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WHY_POLAND.3F_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHY_POLAND.3F-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most visibly, there were numerous improvements in human rights, such as <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet censorship by country">internet freedom</a> (no censorship), civil liberties (1st class) and political rights (1st class), as ranked by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> non-governmental organization. In 1991, Poland became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> and joined the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO) alliance in 1999 along with the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>. Poles then voted to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in <a href="/wiki/Referendums_in_Poland" title="Referendums in Poland">a referendum</a> in June 2003, with <a href="/wiki/Poland_in_the_European_Union" title="Poland in the European Union">Poland becoming a full member</a> on 1 May 2004. Poland joined the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> in 2007, as a result of which, <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Poland" title="Borders of Poland">the country's borders</a> with other member states of the European Union have been dismantled, allowing for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement#European_Union" title="Freedom of movement">full freedom of movement</a> within most of the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-Europe.27s_border-free_zone_expands_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europe.27s_border-free_zone_expands-79">[79]</a></sup> In contrast to this, a section of Poland's eastern border now comprises the external EU border with <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, Russia and Ukraine. That border has become increasingly well protected, and has led in part to the coining of the phrase <a href="/wiki/Fortress_Europe#Modern_times" title="Fortress Europe">'Fortress Europe'</a>, in reference to the seeming 'impossibility' of gaining entry to the EU for citizens of the <a href="/wiki/Former_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Former Soviet Union">former Soviet Union</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_%284%29.jpg/220px-Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_%284%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_%284%29.jpg/330px-Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_%284%29.jpg/440px-Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_National_Tragedy_2010-04-10_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Candles and flowers on the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Route,_Warsaw" title="Royal Route, Warsaw">Royal Route, Warsaw</a> following the <a href="/wiki/2010_Polish_Air_Force_Tu-154_crash" title="2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash">death of Poland's top government officials</a> including <a href="/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski" title="Lech Kaczyński">President</a> in a plane crash over Smolensk in Russia, 10 April 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In an effort to strengthen military cooperation with its neighbors, Poland set up the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Battlegroup" title="Visegrád Battlegroup">Visegrád Battlegroup</a> with Hungary, Czech Republic and Slovakia, with a total of 3,000 troops ready for deployment. Also, in the east Poland created the <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian%E2%80%93Polish%E2%80%93Ukrainian_Brigade" title="Lithuanian–Polish–Ukrainian Brigade">LITPOLUKRBRIG</a> battle groups with Lithuania and Ukraine. These battle groups will operate outside of NATO and within the European defense initiative framework.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 April 2010, the President of the Republic of Poland, <a href="/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski" title="Lech Kaczyński">Lech Kaczyński</a>, along with 89 other high-ranking Polish officials <a href="/wiki/2010_Polish_Air_Force_Tu-154_crash" title="2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash">died in a plane crash</a> near <a href="/wiki/Smolensk" title="Smolensk">Smolensk</a>, Russia. The president's party was on their way to attend an annual service of commemoration for the victims of the <a href="/wiki/Katyn_massacre" title="Katyn massacre">Katyń massacre</a> when the tragedy took place.</p>
<p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a> responsible for the functioning of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council</a> was awarded to Poland. The same year <a href="/wiki/Polish_parliamentary_election,_2011" title="Polish parliamentary election, 2011">parliamentary elections</a> took place in both <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Poland" title="Senate of Poland">the Senate</a> and the Sejm. They were won by the ruling <a href="/wiki/Civic_Platform" title="Civic Platform">Civic Platform</a>. Poland joined <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> in 2012, as well as organised the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> (along with Ukraine). In 2013, Poland also became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Development_Assistance_Committee" title="Development Assistance Committee">Development Assistance Committee</a>. In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland" title="Prime Minister of Poland">Prime Minister of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tusk" title="Donald Tusk">Donald Tusk</a>, was chosen to be <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a>, as resigned as prime minister. The 2015 elections were won by the opposion <a href="/wiki/Law_and_Justice" title="Law and Justice">Law and Justice Party</a> (PiS).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Poland" title="Geography of Poland">Geography of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Poland_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Poland_topo.jpg/220px-Poland_topo.jpg" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Poland_topo.jpg/330px-Poland_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Poland_topo.jpg/440px-Poland_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1364" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Poland_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">Topographic</a> map of Poland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland's territory extends across several geographical regions, between latitudes <a href="/wiki/49th_parallel_north" title="49th parallel north">49°</a> and <a href="/wiki/55th_parallel_north" title="55th parallel north">55° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/14th_meridian_east" title="14th meridian east">14°</a> and <a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_east" title="25th meridian east">25° E</a>. In the north-west is the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic</a> seacoast, which extends from the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pomerania" title="Bay of Pomerania">Bay of Pomerania</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_Bay" title="Gdańsk Bay">Gulf of Gdańsk</a>. This coast is marked by several <a href="/wiki/Spit_(landform)" title="Spit (landform)">spits</a>, coastal lakes (former bays that have been cut off from the sea), and dunes. The largely straight coastline is indented by the <a href="/wiki/Szczecin_Lagoon" title="Szczecin Lagoon">Szczecin Lagoon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Puck" title="Bay of Puck">Bay of Puck</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Lagoon" title="Vistula Lagoon">Vistula Lagoon</a>.</p>
<p>The centre and parts of the north of the country lie within the <a href="/wiki/North_European_Plain" title="North European Plain">North European Plain</a>. Rising above these lowlands is a geographical region comprising four hilly districts of <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">moraines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moraine-dammed_lake" title="Moraine-dammed lake">moraine-dammed lakes</a> formed during and after the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">Pleistocene ice age</a>. These lake districts are the <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomeranian</a> Lake District, the Greater Polish Lake District, the <a href="/wiki/Kashubia" title="Kashubia">Kashubian</a> Lake District, and the <a href="/wiki/Masurian_Lake_District" title="Masurian Lake District">Masurian Lake District</a>. The Masurian Lake District is the largest of the four and covers much of north-eastern Poland. The lake districts form part of the Baltic Ridge, a series of moraine belts along the southern shore of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.</p>
<p>South of the Northern European Plain are the regions of <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Masovia" class="mw-redirect" title="Masovia">Masovia</a>, which are marked by broad ice-age river valleys. Farther south is a mountainous region, including the <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">Sudetes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w-Cz%C4%99stochowa_Upland" title="Kraków-Częstochowa Upland">Kraków-Częstochowa Upland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awi%C4%99tokrzyskie_Mountains" title="Świętokrzyskie Mountains">Świętokrzyskie Mountains</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Beskids" title="Beskids">Beskids</a>. The highest part of the Carpathians is the <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a>, along Poland's southern border.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg/220px-Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg/330px-Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg/440px-Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Widoczek_10062005_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sto%C5%82owe_Mountains" title="Stołowe Mountains">Table Mountains</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">Lower Silesian Voivodeship</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The geological structure of Poland has been shaped by the <a href="/wiki/Continental_collision" title="Continental collision">continental collision</a> of Europe and Africa over the past 60&#160;million years and, more recently, by the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> glaciations of northern Europe. Both processes shaped the <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">Sudetes</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>. The moraine landscape of northern Poland contains soils made up mostly of sand or <a href="/wiki/Loam" title="Loam">loam</a>, while the ice age river valleys of the south often contain <a href="/wiki/Loess" title="Loess">loess</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w-Cz%C4%99stochowa_Upland" title="Kraków-Częstochowa Upland">Kraków-Częstochowa Upland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pieniny" title="Pieniny">Pieniny</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Tatras" title="Western Tatras">Western Tatras</a> consist of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">High Tatras</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Beskids" title="Beskids">Beskids</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Karkonosze" class="mw-redirect" title="Karkonosze">Karkonosze</a> are made up mainly of <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalts</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Polish_Jura_Chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Jura Chain">Polish Jura Chain</a> is one of the oldest mountain ranges on earth.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg/220px-Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg/330px-Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg/440px-Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Giewont_and_Wielka_Turnia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a> in southern Poland average 2,000 metres (6,600 ft) in elevation</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland has 70 mountains over 2,000 metres (6,600 feet) in elevation, all in the <a href="/wiki/Tatras" class="mw-redirect" title="Tatras">Tatras</a>. The Polish Tatras, which consist of the High Tatras and the Western Tatras, is the highest mountain group of Poland and of the entire Carpathian range. In the High Tatras lies Poland's highest point, the north-western summit of <a href="/wiki/Rysy" title="Rysy">Rysy</a>, 2,499 metres (8,199&#160;ft) in elevation. At its foot lies the mountain lakes of <a href="/wiki/Czarny_Staw_pod_Rysami" title="Czarny Staw pod Rysami">Czarny Staw pod Rysami</a> (Black Lake below Mount Rysy), and <a href="/wiki/Morskie_Oko" title="Morskie Oko">Morskie Oko</a> (the Marine Eye).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA.2FWorld_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA.2FWorld-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second highest mountain group in Poland is the <a href="/wiki/Beskids" title="Beskids">Beskids</a>, whose highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Babia_G%C3%B3ra" title="Babia Góra">Babia Góra</a>, at 1,725 metres (5,659&#160;ft). The next highest mountain groups are the <a href="/wiki/Krkono%C5%A1e" title="Krkonoše">Karkonosze</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">Sudetes</a>, the highest point of which is <a href="/wiki/Sn%C4%9B%C5%BEka" title="Sněžka">Śnieżka</a> at 1,603 metres (5,259&#160;ft), and the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Anie%C5%BCnik_Mountains" title="Śnieżnik Mountains">Śnieżnik Mountains</a>, the highest point of which is <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%A1lick%C3%BD_Sn%C4%9B%C5%BEn%C3%ADk" title="Králický Sněžník">Śnieżnik</a> at 1,425 metres (4,675&#160;ft).</p>
<p>Other notable uplands include the <a href="/wiki/Sto%C5%82owe_Mountains" title="Stołowe Mountains">Table Mountains</a>, which are noted for their interesting rock formations, the <a href="/wiki/Bieszczady_Mountains" title="Bieszczady Mountains">Bieszczady Mountains</a> in the far southeast of the country, in which the highest Polish peak is <a href="/wiki/Tarnica" title="Tarnica">Tarnica</a> at 1,346 metres (4,416&#160;ft), the <a href="/wiki/Gorce_Mountains" title="Gorce Mountains">Gorce Mountains</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gorce_National_Park" title="Gorce National Park">Gorce National Park</a>, whose highest point is <a href="/wiki/Turbacz" title="Turbacz">Turbacz</a> at 1,310 metres (4,298&#160;ft), the <a href="/wiki/Pieniny" title="Pieniny">Pieniny</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pieniny_National_Park_(Poland)" title="Pieniny National Park (Poland)">Pieniny National Park</a>, the highest point of which is Wysokie Skałki (Wysoka) at 1,050 metres (3,445&#160;ft), and the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awi%C4%99tokrzyskie_Mountains" title="Świętokrzyskie Mountains">Świętokrzyskie Mountains</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awi%C4%99tokrzyski_National_Park" title="Świętokrzyski National Park">Świętokrzyski National Park</a>, which have two similarly high peaks: <a href="/wiki/%C5%81ysica" title="Łysica">Łysica</a> at 612 metres (2,008&#160;ft) and <a href="/wiki/%C5%81ysa_G%C3%B3ra" title="Łysa Góra">Łysa Góra</a> at 593 metres (1,946&#160;ft).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg/220px-S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg/330px-S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg/440px-S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_Park_Narodowy_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shifting sand dunes in <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_National_Park" title="Słowiński National Park">Słowiński National Park</a> located in northern Poland on the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> coast. Driven by wind, the dunes move at an annual rate of 3 to 10 metres (9.8 to 32.8 ft) per year</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The lowest point in Poland – at 2 metres (6.6&#160;ft) below sea level – is at Raczki Elbląskie, near <a href="/wiki/Elbl%C4%85g" title="Elbląg">Elbląg</a> in the Vistula Delta.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Zag%C5%82%C4%99bie_D%C4%85browskie" title="Zagłębie Dąbrowskie">Zagłębie Dąbrowskie</a> (the Coal Fields of <a href="/wiki/D%C4%85browa_G%C3%B3rnicza" title="Dąbrowa Górnicza">Dąbrowa</a>) region in the <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Silesian Voivodeship">Silesian Voivodeship</a> in southern Poland is an area of sparsely vegetated sand known as the <a href="/wiki/B%C5%82%C4%99d%C3%B3w_Desert" title="Błędów Desert">Błędów Desert</a>. It covers an area of 32 square kilometres (12&#160;sq&#160;mi). It is not a natural desert but results from human activity from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> onwards.</p>
<p>The Baltic Sea activity in <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82owi%C5%84ski_National_Park" title="Słowiński National Park">Słowiński National Park</a> created <a href="/wiki/Sand_dunes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sand dunes">sand dunes</a> which in the course of time separated the bay from the sea creating two lakes. As waves and wind carry sand inland the dunes slowly move, at a rate of 3 to 10 metres (9.8 to 32.8&#160;ft) meters per year. Some dunes reach the height of up to 30 metres (98&#160;ft). The highest peak of the park is Rowokol (115 metres or 377 feet <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waters">Waters</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rivers_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Rivers of Poland">Rivers of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandomierz_(js).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Sandomierz_%28js%29.jpg/220px-Sandomierz_%28js%29.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Sandomierz_%28js%29.jpg/330px-Sandomierz_%28js%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Sandomierz_%28js%29.jpg/440px-Sandomierz_%28js%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5655" data-file-height="3654" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandomierz_(js).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Vistula River">Vistula River</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Sandomierz_Castle" title="Sandomierz Castle">Royal Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sandomierz" title="Sandomierz">Sandomierz</a>. The river is the longest in Poland, flowing the entire length of the country for 1,047 kilometres (651 mi)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The longest rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Vistula River">Vistula</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <span lang="pl"><i>Wisła</i></span>), 1,047 kilometres (651&#160;mi) long; the <a href="/wiki/Oder_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Oder River">Oder</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <span lang="pl"><i>Odra</i></span>) which forms part of Poland's western border, 854 kilometres (531&#160;mi) long; its tributary, the <a href="/wiki/Warta" title="Warta">Warta</a>, 808 kilometres (502&#160;mi) long; and the <a href="/wiki/Bug_River" title="Bug River">Bug</a>, a tributary of the Vistula, 772 kilometres (480&#160;mi) long. The Vistula and the Oder flow into the Baltic Sea, as do numerous smaller rivers in Pomerania.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/%C5%81yna_River" title="Łyna River">Łyna</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Angrapa_River" title="Angrapa River">Angrapa</a> flow by way of the <a href="/wiki/Pregolya" class="mw-redirect" title="Pregolya">Pregolya</a> to the Baltic, and the <a href="/wiki/Czarna_Ha%C5%84cza" title="Czarna Hańcza">Czarna Hańcza</a> flows into the Baltic through the <a href="/wiki/Neman_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Neman River">Neman</a>. While the great majority of Poland's rivers drain into the Baltic Sea, Poland's Beskids are the source of some of the upper tributaries of the <a href="/wiki/Orava_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Orava River">Orava</a>, which flows via the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1h" title="Váh">Váh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The eastern Beskids are also the source of some streams that drain through the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> to the Black Sea.</p>
<p>Poland's rivers have been used since early times for navigation. The <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Vikings</a>, for example, traveled up the Vistula and the Oder in their <a href="/wiki/Longship" title="Longship">longships</a>. In the Middle Ages and in early modern times, when the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth was the breadbasket of Europe;<sup id="cite_ref-Snyder-111_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Snyder-111-83">[83]</a></sup> the shipment of grain and other agricultural products down the Vistula toward <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a> and onward to other parts of Europe took on great importance.<sup id="cite_ref-Snyder-111_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Snyder-111-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg/220px-%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg/330px-%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg/440px-%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C5%81eba_near_%C5%81ebsko_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/%C5%81ebsko_Lake" title="Łebsko Lake">Łebsko Lake</a> is a coastal freshwater <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoon</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a> region</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the valley of <a href="/wiki/Pilica_(river)" title="Pilica (river)">Pilica</a> river in <a href="/wiki/Tomasz%C3%B3w_Mazowiecki" title="Tomaszów Mazowiecki">Tomaszów Mazowiecki</a> there is a unique natural <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">karst spring</a> of water containing calcium salts, that is an object of protection in <a href="/wiki/Niebieskie_%C5%B9r%C3%B3d%C5%82a_Nature_Reserve" title="Niebieskie Źródła Nature Reserve">Niebieskie Źródła Nature Reserve</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sulej%C3%B3w_Landscape_Park" title="Sulejów Landscape Park">Sulejów Landscape Park</a>. The origin of the name of the reserve <i>Niebieskie Źródła</i>, that means <i>Blue Springs</i>, comes from the fact that red waves are absorbed by water and only blue and green are reflected from the bottom of the spring, giving that atypical colour.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>With almost ten thousand closed bodies of water covering more than 1 hectare (2.47 acres) each, Poland has one of the highest numbers of lakes in the world. In Europe, only <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> has a greater density of lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-Walske-28_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walske-28-85">[85]</a></sup> The largest lakes, covering more than 100 square kilometres (39&#160;sq&#160;mi), are <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Aniardwy" title="Śniardwy">Lake Śniardwy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mamry" title="Lake Mamry">Lake Mamry</a> in <a href="/wiki/Masuria" title="Masuria">Masuria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C5%81ebsko_Lake" title="Łebsko Lake">Lake Łebsko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drawsko_Lake" title="Drawsko Lake">Lake Drawsko</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a>.</p>
<p>In addition to the lake districts in the north (in Masuria, Pomerania, <a href="/wiki/Kashubians" title="Kashubians">Kashubia</a>, Lubuskie, and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Poland" title="Greater Poland">Greater Poland</a>), there is also a large number of mountain lakes in the Tatras, of which the Morskie Oko is the largest in area. The lake with the greatest depth—of more than 100 metres (328&#160;ft)—is <a href="/wiki/Ha%C5%84cza" title="Hańcza">Lake Hańcza</a> in the Wigry Lake District, east of Masuria in <a href="/wiki/Podlaskie_Voivodeship" title="Podlaskie Voivodeship">Podlaskie Voivodeship</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg/220px-Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg/330px-Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg/440px-Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="550" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Olecko_Jezioro_Oleckie_Wielkie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Masurian_Lake_District" title="Masurian Lake District">Masurian Lake District</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Masuria" title="Masuria">Masuria</a> region of Poland contains more than 2,000 lakes</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among the first lakes whose shores were settled are those in the Greater Polish Lake District. The <a href="/wiki/Stilt_house" title="Stilt house">stilt house</a> settlement of <a href="/wiki/Biskupin" title="Biskupin">Biskupin</a>, occupied by more than one thousand residents, was founded before the 7th century BC by people of the <a href="/wiki/Lusatian_culture" title="Lusatian culture">Lusatian culture</a>.</p>
<p>Lakes have always played an important role in Polish history and continue to be of great importance to today's modern Polish society. The ancestors of today's Poles, the <a href="/wiki/Polans_(western)" title="Polans (western)">Polanie</a>, built their first fortresses on islands in these lakes. The legendary Prince <a href="/wiki/Popiel" title="Popiel">Popiel</a> ruled from <a href="/wiki/Kruszwica" title="Kruszwica">Kruszwica</a> tower erected on the <a href="/wiki/Gop%C5%82o" title="Gopło">Lake Gopło</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicles-93_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicles-93-86">[86]</a></sup> The first historically documented ruler of Poland, Duke <a href="/wiki/Mieszko_I_of_Poland" title="Mieszko I of Poland">Mieszko I</a>, had his palace on an island in the Warta River in <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84" title="Poznań">Poznań</a>. Nowadays the Polish lakes provide a location for the pursuit of water sports such as <a href="/wiki/Yachting" title="Yachting">yachting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wind-surfing" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind-surfing">wind-surfing</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg/220px-D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg/330px-D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg/440px-D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C4%99bki_1a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Polish <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> coast is approximately 528 kilometres (328 mi) long and extends from <a href="/wiki/Usedom" title="Usedom">Usedom</a> island in the west to <a href="/wiki/Krynica_Morska" title="Krynica Morska">Krynica Morska</a> in the east</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Polish Baltic coast is approximately 528 kilometres (328&#160;mi) long and extends from <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Świnoujście">Świnoujście</a> on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Usedom" title="Usedom">Usedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolin" title="Wolin">Wolin</a> in the west to <a href="/wiki/Krynica_Morska" title="Krynica Morska">Krynica Morska</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Spit" title="Vistula Spit">Vistula Spit</a> in the east. For the most part, Poland has a smooth coastline, which has been shaped by the continual movement of sand by currents and winds. This continual <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deposition_(geology)" title="Deposition (geology)">deposition</a> has formed cliffs, dunes, and spits, many of which have migrated landwards to close off former lagoons, such as Łebsko Lake in Słowiński National Park.</p>
<p>Prior to the end of the Second World War and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland_immediately_after_World_War_II" title="Territorial changes of Poland immediately after World War II">change in national borders</a>, Poland had only a very small coastline; this was situated at the end of the '<a href="/wiki/Polish_Corridor" title="Polish Corridor">Polish Corridor</a>', the only internationally recognised Polish territory which afforded the country access to the sea. However, after World War II, the redrawing of Poland's borders and resulting 'shift' of the country's borders left it with an expanded coastline, thus allowing for far greater access to the sea than was ever previously possible. The significance of this event, and importance of it to Poland's future as a major industrialised nation, was alluded to by the 1945 <a href="/wiki/Poland%27s_Wedding_to_the_Sea" title="Poland's Wedding to the Sea">Wedding to the Sea</a>.</p>
<p>The largest spits are <a href="/wiki/Hel_Peninsula" title="Hel Peninsula">Hel Peninsula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Spit" title="Vistula Spit">Vistula Spit</a>. The largest Polish Baltic island is called <a href="/wiki/Wolin" title="Wolin">Wolin</a>. The largest sea <a href="/wiki/Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour">harbours</a> are <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Szczecin" title="Port of Szczecin">Szczecin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Port of Świnoujście">Świnoujście</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gda%C5%84sk" title="Port of Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gdynia" title="Port of Gdynia">Gdynia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Police" title="Port of Police">Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ko%C5%82obrzeg" title="Port of Kołobrzeg">Kołobrzeg</a> and the main coastal resorts – <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Świnoujście">Świnoujście</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mi%C4%99dzyzdroje" title="Międzyzdroje">Międzyzdroje</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%82obrzeg" title="Kołobrzeg">Kołobrzeg</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%81eba" title="Łeba">Łeba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sopot" title="Sopot">Sopot</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82awowo" title="Władysławowo">Władysławowo</a> and the Hel Peninsula.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_use">Land use</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg/220px-2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg/330px-2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg/440px-2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4028" data-file-height="2668" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Pole_uprawne_w_Raszkowie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">Wheat</a> fields in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Poland" title="Greater Poland">Greater Poland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland is the fourth most forested country in Europe. Forests cover about 30.5% of Poland's land area based on international standards.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_name.3DrapBIP_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_name.3DrapBIP-87">[87]</a></sup> Its overall percentage is still increasing. <a href="/wiki/Forests_of_Poland" title="Forests of Poland">Forests of Poland</a> are managed by the national program of reforestation (KPZL), aiming at an increase of forest-cover to 33% in 2050. The richness of Polish forest (per SoEF 2011 statistics) is more than twice as high as European average (with Germany and France at the top), containing 2.304 billion cubic metres of trees.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_name.3DrapBIP_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_name.3DrapBIP-87">[87]</a></sup> The largest forest complex in Poland is <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Wilderness" title="Lower Silesian Wilderness">Lower Silesian Wilderness</a>.</p>
<p>More than 1% of Poland's territory, 3,145 square kilometres (1,214&#160;sq&#160;mi), is protected within 23 <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national parks of Poland">Polish national parks</a>. Three more national parks are projected for <a href="/wiki/Masuria" title="Masuria">Masuria</a>, the Kraków-Częstochowa Upland, and the eastern <a href="/wiki/Beskids" title="Beskids">Beskids</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> along lakes and rivers in central Poland are legally protected, as are coastal areas in the north. There are over 120 areas designated as <a href="/wiki/Landscape_Park_(Poland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landscape Park (Poland)">landscape parks</a>, along with numerous <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Poland" title="Protected areas of Poland">protected areas</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">Natura 2000</a>).</p>
<p>Since Poland's accession to the European Union in 2004, Polish agriculture has performed extremely well and the country has over two million private farms.<sup id="cite_ref-agEcon_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agEcon-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> It is the leading producer in Europe of potatoes and <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a> (world's second largest in 1989) the world's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Triticale" title="Triticale">triticale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gabrielyan_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabrielyan-90">[90]</a></sup> and one of the more important producers of barley, oats, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beets" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar beets">sugar beets</a>, flax, and fruits. Poland is the European Union's fourth largest supplier of pork after Germany, Spain and France.<sup id="cite_ref-ec.europa.eu_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg/220px-Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg/330px-Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg/440px-Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="912" data-file-height="608" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bia%C5%82owieski_Park_Narodowy03_23a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a>, an ancient woodland in eastern Poland, is now home to 800 wild <a href="/wiki/Wisent" class="mw-redirect" title="Wisent">wisent</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Poland belongs to the Central European province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>, the territory of <a href="/wiki/Ecoregions_in_Poland" title="Ecoregions in Poland">Poland belongs to three Palearctic Ecoregions</a> of the continental forest spanning Central and Northern European <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest">temperate broadleaf and mixed forest</a> ecoregions as well as the Carpathian <a href="/wiki/Montane" class="mw-redirect" title="Montane">montane</a> conifer forest.</p>
<p>Many animals that have since died out in other parts of Europe still survive in Poland, such as the <a href="/wiki/Wisent" class="mw-redirect" title="Wisent">wisent</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_woodland" title="Ancient woodland">ancient woodland</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Podlaskie" class="mw-redirect" title="Podlaskie">Podlaskie</a>. Other such species include the <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bear</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa" title="Białowieża">Białowieża</a>, in the Tatras, and in the Beskids, the <a href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" title="Gray wolf">gray wolf</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">Eurasian lynx</a> in various forests, the <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a> in northern Poland, and the <a href="/wiki/Beaver" title="Beaver">beaver</a> in Masuria, Pomerania, and Podlaskie.</p>
<p>In the forests, one also encounters game animals, such as <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boars</a>. In eastern Poland there are a number of ancient woodlands, like <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Białowieża forest">Białowieża forest</a>, that have never been cleared or have been disturbed much by people. There are also large forested areas in the mountains, Masuria, Pomerania, <a href="/wiki/Lubusz_Land" title="Lubusz Land">Lubusz Land</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesia" title="Lower Silesia">Lower Silesia</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:White_Stork_(Ciconia_ciconia),_Zajki_meadows,_Eastern_Poland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/White_Stork_%28Ciconia_ciconia%29%2C_Zajki_meadows%2C_Eastern_Poland.jpg/220px-White_Stork_%28Ciconia_ciconia%29%2C_Zajki_meadows%2C_Eastern_Poland.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/White_Stork_%28Ciconia_ciconia%29%2C_Zajki_meadows%2C_Eastern_Poland.jpg/330px-White_Stork_%28Ciconia_ciconia%29%2C_Zajki_meadows%2C_Eastern_Poland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/White_Stork_%28Ciconia_ciconia%29%2C_Zajki_meadows%2C_Eastern_Poland.jpg/440px-White_Stork_%28Ciconia_ciconia%29%2C_Zajki_meadows%2C_Eastern_Poland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4058" data-file-height="3043" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:White_Stork_(Ciconia_ciconia),_Zajki_meadows,_Eastern_Poland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Poland is host to the largest white stork population in Europe<sup id="cite_ref-Poland.pl_.E2.80.93_White_Stork_.E2.80.93_About_White_Stork_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poland.pl_.E2.80.93_White_Stork_.E2.80.93_About_White_Stork-92">[92]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland is the most important breeding ground for a variety of European <a href="/wiki/Migratory_birds" class="mw-redirect" title="Migratory birds">migratory birds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-poland.gov.pl-Fauna_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poland.gov.pl-Fauna-93">[93]</a></sup> Out of all of the migratory birds who come to Europe for the summer, one quarter of the global population of <a href="/wiki/White_stork" title="White stork">white storks</a> (40,000 breeding pairs) live in Poland,<sup id="cite_ref-Hillstrom-34_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillstrom-34-94">[94]</a></sup> particularly in the lake districts and the wetlands along the <a href="/wiki/Biebrza" title="Biebrza">Biebrza</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Narew" title="Narew">Narew</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Warta" title="Warta">Warta</a>, which are part of nature reserves or national parks.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<p>The climate is mostly <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">temperate</a> throughout the country. The climate is <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a> in the north and west and becomes gradually warmer and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a> towards the south and east. Summers are generally warm, with average temperatures between 18 and 30&#160;°C (64.4 and 86.0&#160;°F) depending on a region. Winters are rather cold, with average temperatures around 3&#160;°C (37.4&#160;°F) in the northwest and −6&#160;°C (21&#160;°F) in the northeast. <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> falls throughout the year, although, especially in the east; winter is drier than summer.<sup id="cite_ref-Photius_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Photius-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The warmest region in Poland is <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">Lower Silesia</a> located in south-western Poland where temperatures in the summer average between 24 and 32&#160;°C (75 and 90&#160;°F) but can go as high as 34 to 39&#160;°C (93.2 to 102.2&#160;°F) on some days in the warmest month of July and August. The warmest cities in Poland are <a href="/wiki/Tarn%C3%B3w" title="Tarnów">Tarnów</a>, which is situated in <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Poland_Voivodeship" title="Lesser Poland Voivodeship">Lesser Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a>, which is located in Lower Silesia. The average temperatures in Wrocław are 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) in the summer and 0&#160;°C (32.0&#160;°F) in the winter, but <a href="/wiki/Tarn%C3%B3w" title="Tarnów">Tarnów</a> has the longest summer in all of Poland, which lasts for 115 days, from mid-May to mid-September. The coldest region of Poland is in the northeast in the <a href="/wiki/Podlaskie_Voivodeship" title="Podlaskie Voivodeship">Podlaskie Voivodeship</a> near the border of <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>. Usually the coldest city is <a href="/wiki/Suwa%C5%82ki" title="Suwałki">Suwałki</a>. The climate is affected by cold fronts which come from <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. The average temperature in the winter in Podlaskie ranges from −6 to −4&#160;°C (21 to 25&#160;°F). The biggest impact of the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> is observed in <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Świnoujście">Świnoujście</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> seashore area from <a href="/wiki/Police,_Poland" title="Police, Poland">Police</a> to <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82upsk" title="Słupsk">Słupsk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
