<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Poland" title="Politics of Poland">Politics of Poland</a></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:left; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;">
<tr>
<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Prezydent Andrzej Duda podczas Zgromadzenia Narodowego w Poznaniu (cropped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_%28cropped%29.jpg/120px-Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="120" height="153" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-Prezydent_Andrzej_Duda_podczas_Zgromadzenia_Narodowego_w_Poznaniu_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="442" /></a></td>
<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="V4 Prague 2015-12-03 - Viktor Orban 1 (cropped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_%28cropped%29.jpg/119px-V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="119" height="153" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_%28cropped%29.jpg/179px-V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_%28cropped%29.jpg/238px-V4_Prague_2015-12-03_-_Viktor_Orban_1_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="242" data-file-height="312" /></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Duda" title="Andrzej Duda">Andrzej Duda</a><br />
<small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Poland" title="President of Poland">President</a></small></td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Beata_Szyd%C5%82o" title="Beata Szydło">Beata Szydło</a><br />
<small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland" title="Prime Minister of Poland">Prime Minister</a></small></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Poland is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Republic of Poland">president</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, whose current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of the Republic of Poland">constitution</a> dates from 1997. Poland ranks in the top 20 percent of the most peaceful countries in the world, according to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>. The government structure centers on the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of the Republic of Poland">Council of Ministers</a>, led by a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of the Republic of Poland">prime minister</a>. The president appoints the cabinet according to the proposals of the prime minister, typically from the majority coalition in the <a href="/wiki/Sejm_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Sejm of the Republic of Poland">Sejm</a>. The president is elected by popular vote every five years. The current <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Republic of Poland">president</a> is <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Duda" title="Andrzej Duda">Andrzej Duda</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland" title="Prime Minister of Poland">prime minister</a> is <a href="/wiki/Beata_Szyd%C5%82o" title="Beata Szydło">Beata Szydło</a>.</p>
<p>Polish voters elect a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliament consisting of a 460-member lower house (Sejm) and a 100-member Senate (<a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of the Republic of Poland">Senat</a>). The Sejm is elected under <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D'Hondt method">d'Hondt method</a>, a method similar to that used in many parliamentary political systems. The Senat, on the other hand, is elected under the <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post voting</a> method, with one senator being returned from each of the 100 constituencies.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG/220px-Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG/330px-Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG/440px-Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zgromadzenie_Narodowe_4_czerwca_2014_Kancelaria_Senatu_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">Sejm</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a> of the Polish <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the exception of ethnic minority parties, only candidates of <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Poland" title="List of political parties in Poland">political parties</a> receiving at least 5% of the total national vote can enter the Sejm. When sitting in joint session, members of the Sejm and Senat form the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of the Republic of Poland">National Assembly</a> (the <i>Zgromadzenie Narodowe</i>). The National Assembly is formed on three occasions: when a new president takes the <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_office" title="Oath of office">oath of office</a>; when an indictment against the President of the Republic is brought to the State Tribunal (<i>Trybunał Stanu</i>); and when a president's permanent incapacity to exercise his duties due to the state of his health is declared. To date only the first instance has occurred.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial branch</a> plays an important role in decision-making. Its major institutions include the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Court of the Republic of Poland">Supreme Court of the Republic of Poland</a> (<i>Sąd Najwyższy</i>); the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Administrative_Court_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Administrative Court of the Republic of Poland">Supreme Administrative Court of the Republic of Poland</a> (<i>Naczelny Sąd Administracyjny</i>); the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Tribunal_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional Tribunal of the Republic of Poland">Constitutional Tribunal of the Republic of Poland</a> (<i>Trybunał Konstytucyjny</i>); and the <a href="/wiki/State_Tribunal_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="State Tribunal of the Republic of Poland">State Tribunal of the Republic of Poland</a> (<i>Trybunał Stanu</i>). On the approval of the Senat, the Sejm also appoints the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Ombudsman" title="Polish Ombudsman">ombudsman</a> or the Commissioner for Civil Rights Protection (<i>Rzecznik Praw Obywatelskich</i>) for a five-year term. The ombudsman has the duty of guarding the observance and implementation of the rights and liberties of Polish citizens and residents, of the law and of principles of community life and social justice.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Poland" title="Law of Poland">Law of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polishsupremecourt.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Polishsupremecourt.JPEG/170px-Polishsupremecourt.JPEG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Polishsupremecourt.JPEG/255px-Polishsupremecourt.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Polishsupremecourt.JPEG/340px-Polishsupremecourt.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polishsupremecourt.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Poland" title="Supreme Court of Poland">Supreme Court</a> building in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Poland" title="Constitution of Poland">Constitution of Poland</a> is the supreme law in contemporary Poland, and the Polish legal system is based on the principle of civil rights, governed by the code of Civil Law. Historically, the most famous Polish legal act is the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_3_May_1791" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of 3 May 1791">Constitution of 3 May 1791</a>. Historian <a href="/wiki/Norman_Davies" title="Norman Davies">Norman Davies</a> describes it as the first of its kind in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies_699_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies_699-98">[98]</a></sup> The Constitution was instituted as a <a href="/wiki/Government_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Government Act">Government Act</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <span lang="pl"><i>Ustawa rządowa</i></span>) and then adopted on 3 May 1791 by the <a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">Sejm</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>. Primarily, it was designed to redress long-standing political defects of the <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federative</a> Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth and its <a href="/wiki/Golden_Liberty" title="Golden Liberty">Golden Liberty</a>. Previously only the <a href="/wiki/Henrican_articles" class="mw-redirect" title="Henrican articles">Henrican articles</a> signed by each of Poland's elected kings could perform the function of a set of basic laws.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG/170px-Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG/255px-Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG/340px-Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG 2x" data-file-width="554" data-file-height="842" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manuscript_of_the_Constitution_of_the_3rd_May_1791.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_May_3,_1791" title="Constitution of May 3, 1791"><i>Constitution of May 3rd</i></a> adopted in 1791 was the first modern constitution in Europe<sup id="cite_ref-Davies_699_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies_699-98">[98]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The new Constitution introduced political equality between <a href="/wiki/Townspeople" class="mw-redirect" title="Townspeople">townspeople</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">szlachta</a></i>), and placed the <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasants</a> under the protection of the government. The Constitution abolished pernicious parliamentary institutions such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Liberum_veto" title="Liberum veto">liberum veto</a></i>, which at one time had placed the <a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">sejm</a> at the mercy of any deputy who might choose, or be <a href="/wiki/Bribery" title="Bribery">bribed</a> by an interest or foreign power, to have rescinded all the legislation that had been passed by that sejm. The 3 May Constitution sought to supplant the existing anarchy fostered by some of the country's <a href="/wiki/Reactionary" title="Reactionary">reactionary</a> <a href="/wiki/Magnate" title="Magnate">magnates</a>, with a more <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a> and democratic <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>. The adoption of <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Constitution_of_3_May_1791" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Constitution of 3 May 1791">the constitution</a> was treated as a threat by Poland's neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-Gierowski_251_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gierowski_251-99">[99]</a></sup> In response <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, Austria and Russia formed an anti-Polish alliance and over the next decade collaborated with one another to <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">partition</a> their weaker neighbour and destroyed the Polish state. In the words of two of its co-authors, <a href="/wiki/Ignacy_Potocki" title="Ignacy Potocki">Ignacy Potocki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ko%C5%82%C5%82%C4%85taj" title="Hugo Kołłątaj">Hugo Kołłątaj</a>, the constitution represented "the last will and testament of the expiring Fatherland." Despite this, its text influenced many later <a href="/wiki/Democratic_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic movement">democratic movements</a> across the globe.<sup id="cite_ref-nd_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nd-100">[100]</a></sup> In Poland, freedom of expression is guaranteed by the Article 25 (section I. The Republic) and Article 54 (section II. The Freedoms, Rights and Obligations of Persons and Citizens) of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Poland" title="Constitution of Poland">Constitution of Poland</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg/140px-Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg" width="140" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg/210px-Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg/280px-Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="4267" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manor_of_Kraszewski_family_in_Roman%C3%B3w_-_Exhibition_hall_-_18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Narcyza_%C5%BBmichowska" title="Narcyza Żmichowska">Narcyza Żmichowska</a> was a proponent of early <a href="/wiki/Feminism_in_Poland" title="Feminism in Poland">feminism in Poland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Feminism_in_Poland" title="Feminism in Poland">Feminism in Poland</a> started in the 1800s in the age of the foreign Partitions. Poland's precursor of feminism, <a href="/wiki/Narcyza_%C5%BBmichowska" title="Narcyza Żmichowska">Narcyza Żmichowska</a>, founded a group of <a href="/wiki/Suffragettes" class="mw-redirect" title="Suffragettes">Suffragettes</a> in 1842. Prior to the <a href="/wiki/Third_Partition_of_Poland" title="Third Partition of Poland">last Partition</a> in 1795, tax-paying females were allowed to take part in political life. Since 1918, following the return to independence, all women could vote. Poland was the 15th (12th sovereign) country to introduce universal women's suffrage. Currently, in Poland abortion is allowed only in special circumstances, such as when the woman's life or health is endangered by the continuation of pregnancy, when the pregnancy is a result of a criminal act, or when the fetus is seriously malformed.<sup id="cite_ref-cpk.org_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpk.org-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurotopics_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurotopics-102">[102]</a></sup> Homosexuality in Poland was confirmed as legal in 1932. Poland recognises gender change.<sup id="cite_ref-ilga-europe.org_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilga-europe.org-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg/220px-Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg/330px-Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="345" data-file-height="229" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marsz_dla_zycia_i_rodziny_2007_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/March_for_Life_and_Family" title="March for Life and Family">March for Life and Family</a> organized in support of <a href="/wiki/Traditional_values" class="mw-redirect" title="Traditional values">traditional social values</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A 2010 article in <i><a href="/wiki/Rzeczpospolita_(newspaper)" title="Rzeczpospolita (newspaper)">Rzeczpospolita</a></i> reported that in a 2008 study three-quarters of Poles were against gay marriage and the adoption of children by gay couples.<sup id="cite_ref-rp.pl450884_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rp.pl450884-104">[104]</a></sup> The same study revealed that 66% of respondents were opposed to <a href="/wiki/Pride_parade" title="Pride parade">Pride parade</a> as the demonstration of a way of life, and 69% believed that gay people should not show their sexual orientation in public.<sup id="cite_ref-interia.2FPolska_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interia.2FPolska-105">[105]</a></sup> Poland belongs to the group of 'Tier 1'<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> (countries whose governments fully comply with the TVPA's minimum standards.) in <a href="/wiki/Trafficking_in_Persons_Report" title="Trafficking in Persons Report">Trafficking in Persons Report</a>. Trafficking women is 'illegal and rare' (top results worldwide).<sup id="cite_ref-WomanStats2011_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WomanStats2011-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Poland's current constitution was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Poland">National Assembly of Poland</a> on 2 April 1997, approved by a national referendum on 25 May 1997, and came into effect on 17 October 1997. It guarantees a multi-party state, the freedoms of religion, speech and assembly, and specifically casts off many Communist ideals to create a '<a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">economic system</a>'. It requires public officials to pursue ecologically sound public policy and acknowledges the inviolability of the home, the right to form trade unions, and to strike, whilst at the same time prohibiting the practices of forced medical experimentation, torture and corporal punishment.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Poland" title="Foreign relations of Poland">Foreign relations of Poland</a></div>
<p>In recent years, Poland has extended its responsibilities and position in European and international affairs, supporting and establishing friendly relations with other European nations and a large number of 'developing' countries.</p>
<p>Poland is a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/G6_(EU)" title="G6 (EU)">G6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">Council of the Baltic Sea States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Triangle" title="Weimar Triangle">Weimar Triangle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a>.</p>
<p>In 1994, Poland became an associate member of the European Union (EU) and its defensive arm, the <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Union" title="Western European Union">Western European Union</a> (WEU), having submitted preliminary documentation for full membership in 1996, it formally joined the European Union in May 2004, along with the other members of the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Visegrád group">Visegrád group</a>. In 1996, Poland achieved full <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a> membership, and at the 1997 Madrid Summit was invited to join the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organisation">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a> (NATO) in the first wave of <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">policy enlargement</a> finally becoming a full member of NATO in March 1999.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG/220px-Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG/330px-Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG/440px-Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4095" data-file-height="2958" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ministerstwo_Spraw_Zagraniczych_al._Szucha_23.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Poland)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Poland)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As changes since the fall of Communism in 1989 have redrawn the map of Europe, Poland has tried to forge strong and mutually beneficial relationships with its seven new neighbours, this has notably included signing 'friendship treaties' to replace links severed by the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. Poland has forged a special relationships with <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-grushenko_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grushenko-108">[108]</a></sup> with whom it co-hosted the UEFA <a href="/wiki/Euro_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a> football tournament, in an effort to firmly anchor the country within the Western world and provide it with an alternative to aligning itself with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>. Despite many positive developments in the region, Poland has found itself in a position where it must seek to defend the rights of ethnic Poles living in the <a href="/wiki/Former_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Former Soviet Union">former Soviet Union</a>; this is particularly true of <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, where in 2005 the <a href="/wiki/Lukashenko" class="mw-redirect" title="Lukashenko">Lukashenko</a> regime launched a campaign against the Polish ethnic minority.<sup id="cite_ref-Bordering_on_madness:_Belarus_mistreats_its_Polish_minority_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bordering_on_madness:_Belarus_mistreats_its_Polish_minority-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Poland is the sixth most populous member state of the European Union and has a grand total of 51 representatives in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>. Ever since joining the union in 2004, successive Polish governments have pursued policies to increase the country's role in European and regional affairs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Poland" title="Administrative divisions of Poland">Administrative divisions of Poland</a></div>
<p>Poland's current <a href="/wiki/Voivodeships_of_Poland" title="Voivodeships of Poland">voivodeships</a> (provinces) are largely based on the country's historic regions, whereas those of the past two decades (to 1998) had been centred on and named for individual cities. The new units range in area from less than 10,000 square kilometres (3,900&#160;sq&#160;mi) for Opole Voivodeship to more than 35,000 square kilometres (14,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) for Masovian Voivodeship. Administrative authority at voivodeship level is shared between a government-appointed <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">voivode</a> (governor), an elected regional assembly (<i><a href="/wiki/Voivodeship_sejmik" title="Voivodeship sejmik">sejmik</a></i>) and an executive elected by that assembly.</p>
<p>The voivodeships are subdivided into <i><a href="/wiki/Powiat" title="Powiat">powiats</a></i> (often referred to in English as counties), and these are further divided into <i><a href="/wiki/Gmina" title="Gmina">gminas</a></i> (also known as communes or municipalities). Major cities normally have the status of both <i>gmina</i> and <i>powiat</i>. Poland has 16 voivodeships, 379 powiats (including 65 cities with <i>powiat</i> status), and 2,478 <i>gminas</i>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces" title="Polish Armed Forces">Polish Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Defence_Force_(Poland)" title="Territorial Defence Force (Poland)">Territorial Defence Force (Poland)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_(48).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_%2848%29.jpg/220px-F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_%2848%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_%2848%29.jpg/330px-F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_%2848%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_%2848%29.jpg/440px-F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_%2848%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:F-16_Jastrz%C4%85b_(48).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Polish_Air_Force" title="Polish Air Force">Polish Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/F-16_Fighting_Falcon" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16s</a>—a single-engine <a href="/wiki/Multirole_combat_aircraft" title="Multirole combat aircraft">multirole</a> <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighter aircraft</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Polish armed forces are composed of four branches: <a href="/wiki/Polish_Land_Forces" title="Polish Land Forces">Land Forces</a> (<i>Wojska Lądowe</i>), <a href="/wiki/Polish_Navy" title="Polish Navy">Navy</a> (<i>Marynarka Wojenna</i>), <a href="/wiki/Polish_Air_Force" title="Polish Air Force">Air Force</a> (<i>Siły Powietrzne</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Special_forces_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Special forces of Poland">Special Forces</a> (<i>Wojska Specjalne</i>). The military is subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of National Defence of the Republic of Poland">Minister for National Defence</a>. However, its commander-in-chief is the President of the Republic. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Defence_Force_(Poland)" title="Territorial Defence Force (Poland)">Territorial Defence Force</a> is a planned military reserve component of the Polish armed forces that, as of 2016, is in the process of being formed. Plans call for the force, once fully active, to consist of 53,000 reservists who will be trained and equipped to counter potential <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_warfare" title="Hybrid warfare">hybrid warfare</a> threats.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Polish army consists of 65,000 active personnel, whilst the navy and air force respectively employ 14,300 and 26,126 servicemen and women. The Polish Navy primarily operates in the Baltic Sea and conducts operations such as maritime patrol, search and rescue for the section of the Baltic under Polish sovereignty, as well as hydrographic measurements and research. Also, the Polish Navy played a more international role as part of the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, providing logistical support for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>. The current position of the Polish Air Force is much the same; it has routinely taken part in <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Air_Policing" title="Baltic Air Policing">Baltic Air Policing</a> assignments, but otherwise, with the exception of a number of units serving in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, has seen no active combat since the end of the Second World War. In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/F-16_Fighting_Falcon" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16C</a> Block 52 was chosen as the new general multi-role fighter for the air force, the first deliveries taking place in November 2006.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_(10710349373).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_%2810710349373%29.jpg/220px-Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_%2810710349373%29.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_%2810710349373%29.jpg/330px-Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_%2810710349373%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_%2810710349373%29.jpg/440px-Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_%2810710349373%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7322" data-file-height="4727" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ex_STEADFAST_JAZZ_(10710349373).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Crew of a <a href="/wiki/KTO_Rosomak" title="KTO Rosomak">KTO Rosomak</a> <a href="/wiki/Armoured_personnel_carrier" title="Armoured personnel carrier">armored personnel carrier</a> during a <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> exercise at the Military Training Area near <a href="/wiki/Drawsko_Pomorskie" title="Drawsko Pomorskie">Drawsko Pomorskie</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most important mission of the armed forces is the defence of Polish territorial integrity and Polish interests abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-mil_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mil-111">[111]</a></sup> Poland's national security goal is to further integrate with <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and European defence, economic, and political institutions through the modernisation and reorganisation of its military.<sup id="cite_ref-mil_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mil-111">[111]</a></sup> The armed forces are being re-organised according to NATO standards, and since 2010, the transition to an entirely contract-based military has been completed. Compulsory military service for men was discontinued in 2008. From 2007, until conscription ended in 2008, the mandatory service was nine months.<sup id="cite_ref-Poland_ends_army_conscription_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poland_ends_army_conscription-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg/220px-%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg/330px-%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg/440px-%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%86wiczenia_3_Flotylli_Okr%C4%99t%C3%B3w_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kaman_SH-2G_Super_Seasprite" title="Kaman SH-2G Super Seasprite">Super Seasprite</a> ship-based helicopter flying by the <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigate</a> <a href="/wiki/ORP_Genera%C5%82_Kazimierz_Pu%C5%82aski" title="ORP Generał Kazimierz Pułaski">ORP Generał Kazimierz Pułaski</a> during an exercise in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Polish military doctrine reflects the same defensive nature as that of its NATO partners. From 1953 to 2009 Poland was a large contributor to various United Nations peacekeeping missions.<sup id="cite_ref-mil_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mil-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Polska_zako.C5.84czy.C5.82a_udzia.C5.82_w_misjach_po_auspicjami_ONZ_.E2.80.93_Wiadomo.C5.9Bci_z_kraju_i_ze_.C5.9Bwiata_.E2.80.93_Gazeta_Prawna_.E2.80.93_Partner_pracodawcy.2C_narz.C4.99dzie_specjalisty_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polska_zako.C5.84czy.C5.82a_udzia.C5.82_w_misjach_po_auspicjami_ONZ_.E2.80.93_Wiadomo.C5.9Bci_z_kraju_i_ze_.C5.9Bwiata_.E2.80.93_Gazeta_Prawna_.E2.80.93_Partner_pracodawcy.2C_narz.C4.99dzie_specjalisty-113">[113]</a></sup> The Polish Armed Forces took part in the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, deploying 2,500 soldiers in the south of that country and commanding the 17-nation <a href="/wiki/Multinational_force_in_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Multinational force in Iraq">Multinational force in Iraq</a>.</p>
<p>The military was temporarily, but severely, affected by the <a href="/wiki/2010_Polish_Air_Force_Tu-154_crash" title="2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash">2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash</a>, which killed the Chief of the Army's General Staff <a href="/wiki/Franciszek_G%C4%85gor" title="Franciszek Gągor">Franciszek Gągor</a> and Air Force commanding general <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_B%C5%82asik" title="Andrzej Błasik">Andrzej Błasik</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-Accident_Database_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Accident_Database-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Senior_Polish_figures_killed_in_plane_crash_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Senior_Polish_figures_killed_in_plane_crash-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Currently, Poland's military is going through a significant modernization phase, which will be completed in 2022. The government plans to spend up to 130 billion złoty (US $34 billion)—however, the final total may reach 235 billion złoty (US $62 billion)—to replace dated equipment and purchase new weapons systems.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Under the program, the military plans to purchase new tracked <a href="/wiki/Armoured_personnel_carriers" class="mw-redirect" title="Armoured personnel carriers">armoured personnel carriers</a>, self-propelled <a href="/wiki/Howitzers" class="mw-redirect" title="Howitzers">howitzers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utility_helicopter" title="Utility helicopter">utility</a> and <a href="/wiki/Attack_helicopter" title="Attack helicopter">attack</a> helicopters, a mid-range <a href="/wiki/Surface-to-air_missile" title="Surface-to-air missile">surface-to-air missile</a> system, <a href="/wiki/Attack_submarines" class="mw-redirect" title="Attack submarines">attack submarines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minehunters" class="mw-redirect" title="Minehunters">minehunters</a>, and coastal <a href="/wiki/Anti-ship_missiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-ship missiles">anti-ship missiles</a>. Also, the army plans to modernize its existing inventory of <a href="/wiki/Main_battle_tanks" class="mw-redirect" title="Main battle tanks">main battle tanks</a>, and update its stock of <a href="/wiki/Small_arms" title="Small arms">small arms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_emergency_services">Law enforcement and emergency services</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Poland" title="Law enforcement in Poland">Law enforcement in Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emergency_medical_services_in_Poland" title="Emergency medical services in Poland">Emergency medical services in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg/170px-Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg/255px-Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg/340px-Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1475" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Silesian_Park_-_Mounted_police_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mounted <a href="/wiki/Policja" title="Policja">Police</a> officers in the <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Park" title="Silesian Park">Silesian Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland has a highly developed system of law enforcement with a long history of effective policing by the <a href="/wiki/Policja" title="Policja">State Police Service</a>. The structure of law enforcement agencies within Poland is a multi-tier one, with the State Police providing criminal-investigative services, <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Police">Municipal Police</a> serving to maintain public order and a number of other specialised agencies, such as the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Border_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Border Guard">Polish Border Guard</a>, acting to fulfil their assigned missions. In addition to these state services, private security companies are also common, although they possess no powers assigned to state agencies, such as, for example, the power to make an arrest or detain a suspect.</p>
<p>Emergency services in Poland consist of the <a href="/wiki/Emergency_medical_services_in_Poland" title="Emergency medical services in Poland">emergency medical services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue#Poland" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a> units of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces" title="Polish Armed Forces">Polish Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_Fire_Service" title="State Fire Service">State Fire Service</a>. Emergency medical services in Poland are, unlike other services, provided for by local and regional government.</p>
<p>Since joining the European Union all of Poland's emergency services have been undergoing major restructuring and have, in the process, acquired large amounts of new equipment and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-.E2.80.93_15_tys._zimowych_mundur.C3.B3w_trafi_do_jednostek_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.E2.80.93_15_tys._zimowych_mundur.C3.B3w_trafi_do_jednostek-119">[119]</a></sup> All emergency services personnel are now uniformed and can be easily recognised. In addition, the police and other agencies have been steadily replacing and modernising their fleets of vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-Nowe_radiowozy_dla_policji_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nowe_radiowozy_dla_policji-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Poland" title="Economy of Poland">Economy of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg/400px-Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg" width="400" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg/600px-Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg/800px-Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4304" data-file-height="1941" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_ul._Emilii_Plater_w_Warszawie_radek_ko%C5%82akowski.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> is the financial and economic hub of Poland.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland's economy is considered to be one of the more resilient of the post-Communist countries and is one of the fastest growing within the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Having a strong domestic market, low private debt, flexible currency, and not being dependent on a single export sector, Poland is the only European economy to have avoided the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">late-2000s recession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Global_Competitiveness_Report_2010.E2.80.932011_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Global_Competitiveness_Report_2010.E2.80.932011-122">[122]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">fall of the communist government</a>, Poland has pursued a policy <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">of liberalising</a> the economy. It is an example of the transition from a <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">centrally planned</a> to a primarily <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market-based economy</a>. The country's most successful exports include machinery, furniture, food products, clothing, shoes and cosmetics.<sup id="cite_ref-Polska-zywnosc_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polska-zywnosc-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-partnerzy2014_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnerzy2014-124">[124]</a></sup> Poland's largest trading partner is Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Euro-Dane_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euro-Dane-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schengenzone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/220px-Schengenzone.svg.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/330px-Schengenzone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/440px-Schengenzone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schengenzone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Poland is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> and the EU <a href="/wiki/Internal_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal market">single market</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> of small and medium state-owned companies and a liberal law on establishing new firms have allowed the development of the private sector. Also, several <a href="/wiki/Consumer_protection" title="Consumer protection">consumer rights</a> organizations have become active in the country. Restructuring and privatisation of "sensitive sectors" such as coal, steel, rail transport and energy has been continuing since 1990. The biggest privatisations have been the sale of the national telecoms firm <a href="/wiki/Orange_Polska" title="Orange Polska">Telekomunikacja Polska</a> to <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">France Télécom</a> in 2000, and an issue of 30% of the shares in Poland's largest bank, <a href="/wiki/PKO_Bank_Polski" class="mw-redirect" title="PKO Bank Polski">PKO Bank Polski</a>, on the Polish stockmarket in 2004.</p>
<p>Poland is recognised as having an economy with development potential, overtaking the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> in mid-2010 to become Europe's sixth largest economy.<sup id="cite_ref-fDi:_Poland_Primed_for_Golden_Decade_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fDi:_Poland_Primed_for_Golden_Decade-126">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Direct_Investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Direct Investment">Foreign Direct Investment</a> in Poland has remained steady ever since the country's political transformation following the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Round_Table_Agreement" title="Polish Round Table Agreement">Round Table Agreement</a> in 1989. However, problems still exist—it is believed that progress of privatization was uneven across sectors due to emergence of interest groups supporting government's push for the reforms based on <i>feasibility</i> rather than <i>efficiency</i>, at the cost of Poland's remaining sectors in need of development and modernisation, such as the extractive industries.<sup id="cite_ref-Kozarzewski_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kozarzewski-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Polish banking sector is the largest in East Central/Eastern European region,<sup id="cite_ref-TWI-2011_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWI-2011-128">[128]</a></sup> with 32.3 branches per 100,000 adults.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank.org_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank.org-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-datatopics.2Fpoland_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-datatopics.2Fpoland-130">[130]</a></sup> The banks are the largest and most developed sector of the country's <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a>. They are regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Supervision_Authority_(Poland)" title="Financial Supervision Authority (Poland)">Polish Financial Supervision Authority</a>. During the transformation to a market-oriented economy, the government privatized several banks, recapitalized the rest, and introduced legal reforms that made the sector more competitive. This has attracted a significant number of strategic foreign investors (ICFI). Poland's banking sector has approximately 5 national banks, a network of nearly 600 cooperative banks and 18 branches of foreign-owned banks. In addition, foreign investors have controlling stakes in nearly 40 commercial banks, which make up 68% of the banking capital.<sup id="cite_ref-TWI-2011_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWI-2011-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:220px;max-width:220px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Stocznia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Stocznia.jpg/218px-Stocznia.jpg" width="218" height="145" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Stocznia.jpg/327px-Stocznia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Stocznia.jpg/436px-Stocznia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="425" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Szczecin" title="Port of Szczecin">Port</a> of <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Szczecin</a> serves 16.5% of all cargo traffic in Polish seaports.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:220px;max-width:220px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg/218px-Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg" width="218" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg/327px-Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg/436px-Container_terminals_in_Gdynia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5228" data-file-height="2399" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gdynia" title="Port of Gdynia">Port</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gdynia" title="Gdynia">Gdynia</a> is one of the largest harbours on the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland has a large number of private farms in its agricultural sector, with the potential to become a leading producer of food in the European Union. The biggest money-makers abroad include smoked and fresh fish, fine chocolate, and dairy products, meats and specialty breads,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> with the exchange rate conducive to export growth.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Food exports amounted to 62 billion <a href="/wiki/Zloty" class="mw-redirect" title="Zloty">zloty</a> in 2011, increasing by 17% from 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Structural reforms in health care, education, the pension system, and state administration have resulted in larger-than-expected fiscal pressures. Warsaw leads Central Europe in foreign investment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> GDP growth had been strong and steady from 1993 to 2000 with only a short slowdown from 2001 to 2002.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> data, Polish PPS GDP per capita stood at 67% of the EU average in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-biznes.pl_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biznes.pl-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Average salaries in the enterprise sector in December 2010 were 3,848 PLN (1,012 euro or 1,374 US dollars)<sup id="cite_ref-Communication_on_the_average_monthly_salary_in_enterprise_sector_excluding_payments_from_profit_awards_in_December_2010_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Communication_on_the_average_monthly_salary_in_enterprise_sector_excluding_payments_from_profit_awards_in_December_2010-135">[135]</a></sup> and growing sharply.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_Economic_Outlook_No._82_.E2.80.93_Poland_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD_Economic_Outlook_No._82_.E2.80.93_Poland-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2017)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Salaries vary between the regions: the median wage in the capital city Warsaw was 4,603 PLN (1,177 euro or 1,680 US dollars) while in <a href="/wiki/Kielce" title="Kielce">Kielce</a> it was 3,083 PLN (788 euro or 1125 US dollars). There is a wide distribution of salaries among the various districts of Poland. They range from 2,020 PLN (517 euro or 737 US dollars) in <a href="/wiki/K%C4%99pno_County" title="Kępno County">Kępno County</a>, which is located in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Poland_Voivodeship" title="Greater Poland Voivodeship">Greater Poland Voivodeship</a> to 5,616 (1,436 euro or 2,050 US dollars) in <a href="/wiki/Lubin_County" title="Lubin County">Lubin County</a>, which lies in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">Lower Silesian Voivodeship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Statistic_Office_of_Poland.28GUS.29_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistic_Office_of_Poland.28GUS.29-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the opening of the labor market in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, Poland experienced a <a href="/wiki/21st_century_economic_migration_of_Poles" class="mw-redirect" title="21st century economic migration of Poles">mass emigration</a> of over 2.3 million abroad, mainly due to higher wages offered abroad, and due to the raise in levels of <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_in_Poland" title="Unemployment in Poland">unemployment</a> following the global <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a> of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-140">[140]</a></sup> The out migration has increased the average wages for the workers who remained in Poland, in particular for those with intermediate level skills.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solaris_Bolechowo_(003).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Solaris_Bolechowo_%28003%29.jpg/220px-Solaris_Bolechowo_%28003%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Solaris_Bolechowo_%28003%29.jpg/330px-Solaris_Bolechowo_%28003%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Solaris_Bolechowo_%28003%29.jpg/440px-Solaris_Bolechowo_%28003%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solaris_Bolechowo_(003).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Solaris_Bus_%26_Coach" title="Solaris Bus &amp; Coach">Solaris Bus &amp; Coach</a> is a family-owned bus, coach and tram manufacturer near <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84" title="Poznań">Poznań</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Products and goods manufactured in Poland include: electronics, buses and trams (<a href="/wiki/Solaris_Bus_%26_Coach" title="Solaris Bus &amp; Coach">Solaris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solbus" title="Solbus">Solbus</a>), helicopters and planes (<a href="/wiki/PZL_%C5%9Awidnik" class="mw-redirect" title="PZL Świdnik">PZL Świdnik</a>, <a href="/wiki/PZL_Mielec" title="PZL Mielec">PZL Mielec</a>), trains (<a href="/wiki/Pesa_SA" title="Pesa SA">Pesa SA</a>), ships (<a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_Shipyard" title="Gdańsk Shipyard">Gdańsk Shipyard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Szczecin_Shipyard" title="Szczecin Shipyard">Szczecin Shipyard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Navy_Shipyard" title="Polish Navy Shipyard">Gdynia Polish Navy Shipyard</a>), military equipment (<a href="/wiki/FB_%22%C5%81ucznik%22_Radom" title="FB &quot;Łucznik&quot; Radom">FB "Łucznik" Radom</a>, <a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bumar_%C5%81ab%C4%99dy" class="extiw" title="pl:Bumar Łabędy">Bumar-Łabędy SA</a>), medicines (<a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zak%C5%82ady_Farmaceutyczne_Polpharma" class="extiw" title="pl:Zakłady Farmaceutyczne Polpharma">Polpharma</a>, <a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polfa_Warszawa" class="extiw" title="pl:Polfa Warszawa">Polfa</a>), food (<a href="/wiki/Tymbark_(company)" title="Tymbark (company)">Tymbark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hortex" title="Hortex">Hortex</a>, <a href="/wiki/E._Wedel" title="E. Wedel">E. Wedel</a>), clothes (<a href="/wiki/LPP_(company)" title="LPP (company)">LLP</a>), glass, pottery (<a href="/wiki/Boleslawiec_Pottery" class="mw-redirect" title="Boleslawiec Pottery">Bolesławiec</a>), chemical products and others.</p>
<p>Poland is also one of the world's biggest producers of <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rape_seed" class="mw-redirect" title="Rape seed">rape seed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">apples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strawberries" class="mw-redirect" title="Strawberries">strawberries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ribes" title="Ribes">ribes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporations">Corporations</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw8gh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Warsaw8gh.jpg/220px-Warsaw8gh.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Warsaw8gh.jpg/330px-Warsaw8gh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Warsaw8gh.jpg/440px-Warsaw8gh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw8gh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a> is one of East-Central Europe's largest exchanges by market capitalization.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland is recognised as a regional economic leader within East-Central Europe, with nearly 40 percent of the 500 biggest companies in the region (by revenues) as well as a <a href="/wiki/Globalisation_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Globalisation index">high globalisation rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Polish_economy_seen_as_stable_and_competitive_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polish_economy_seen_as_stable_and_competitive-143">[143]</a></sup> The country's largest firms comprise the <a href="/wiki/WIG30" title="WIG30">WIG30</a> index, which is traded on the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a>.</p>
<p>Well known Polish brands include, among others <a href="/wiki/PKO_Bank_Polski" class="mw-redirect" title="PKO Bank Polski">PKO BP</a>, <a href="/wiki/PKN_Orlen" title="PKN Orlen">PKN Orlen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polska_Grupa_Energetyczna" title="Polska Grupa Energetyczna">PGE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Powszechny_Zak%C5%82ad_Ubezpiecze%C5%84" title="Powszechny Zakład Ubezpieczeń">PZU</a>, <a href="/wiki/PGNiG" title="PGNiG">PGNiG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tauron_Group" title="Tauron Group">Tauron Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grupa_Lotos" title="Grupa Lotos">Lotos Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/KGHM_Polska_Mied%C5%BA" title="KGHM Polska Miedź">KGHM Polska Miedź</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asseco" title="Asseco">Asseco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plus_(telecommunications_Poland)" title="Plus (telecommunications Poland)">Plus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Play_(telecommunications)" title="Play (telecommunications)">Play</a>, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">PLL LOT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poczta_Polska" title="Poczta Polska">Poczta Polska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_State_Railways" title="Polish State Railways">PKP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biedronka" title="Biedronka">Biedronka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telewizja_Polska" title="Telewizja Polska">TVP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dziennikbudowy_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dziennikbudowy-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
