<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Poland" title="Tourism in Poland">Tourism in Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_of_Poland" title="List of World Heritage Sites of Poland">List of World Heritage Sites of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Historic_Monuments_(Poland)" title="List of Historic Monuments (Poland)">List of Historic Monuments (Poland)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_Poland" title="Seven Wonders of Poland">Seven Wonders of Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Polish_Mountains" title="Crown of Polish Mountains">Crown of Polish Mountains</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afrykarium_tunel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Afrykarium_tunel.jpg/220px-Afrykarium_tunel.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Afrykarium_tunel.jpg/330px-Afrykarium_tunel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Afrykarium_tunel.jpg/440px-Afrykarium_tunel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="1499" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afrykarium_tunel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aquarium in the <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Zoo" title="Wrocław Zoo">Zoological Garden</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland experienced an increase in the number of tourists after joining the European Union in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Travel_And_Tourism_in_Poland_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_And_Tourism_in_Poland-146">[146]</a></sup> Tourism contributes significantly to Poland's overall economy and makes up a relatively large proportion of the country's service market.<sup id="cite_ref-unwto.org.2Fen.2Fpress-release_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unwto.org.2Fen.2Fpress-release-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg/220px-Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg/330px-Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg/440px-Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1392" data-file-height="933" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ratusz_Zamosc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Zamo%C5%9B%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Old City of Zamość">Old City of Zamość</a> is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marienburg_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marienburg_2004.jpg/220px-Marienburg_2004.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marienburg_2004.jpg/330px-Marienburg_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Marienburg_2004.jpg/440px-Marienburg_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marienburg_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Malbork_Castle" title="Malbork Castle">Malbork Castle</a> is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> <a href="/wiki/Brick_gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Brick gothic">brick gothic</a> complex and a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> was the former capital and a relic of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Poland's Golden Age</a> of Renaissance. The city served as the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Road,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Royal Road, Kraków">place of coronation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Royal_coronations_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal coronations in Poland">most Polish kings</a>. <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a> is one of the oldest cities in Poland and possesses a huge market square with two town halls, as well as the oldest <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Zoo" title="Wrocław Zoo">Zoological Gardens</a> with one of the world's largest number of animal species and is famous for its <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw%27s_dwarfs" title="Wrocław's dwarfs">dwarfs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town</a> of Poland's capital, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, was reconstructed after <a href="/wiki/Planned_destruction_of_Warsaw" title="Planned destruction of Warsaw">its wartime destruction</a>. Other cities attracting tourists include <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84" title="Poznań">Poznań</a>, <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Szczecin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lublin" title="Lublin">Lublin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toru%C5%84" title="Toruń">Toruń</a>. The historic site of the Nazi-German <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a> concentration camp is located near <a href="/wiki/O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cim" title="Oświęcim">Oświęcim</a>.</p>
<p>Poland is the 16th most visited country in the world by foreign tourists, as ranked by World Tourism Organization (<a href="/wiki/UNWTO" class="mw-redirect" title="UNWTO">UNWTO</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-UNWTO_Barom12_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNWTO_Barom12-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Poland's main tourist offerings include outdoor activities such as skiing, sailing and mountain hiking, as well as agrotourism, sightseeing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Historic_Monuments_(Poland)" title="List of Historic Monuments (Poland)">historical monuments</a>. Tourist destinations include the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> coast in the north; the <a href="/wiki/Masurian_Lake_District" title="Masurian Lake District">Masurian Lake District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a> in the east; on the south <a href="/wiki/Karkonosze" class="mw-redirect" title="Karkonosze">Karkonosze</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Table_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Table Mountains">Table Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Rysy" title="Rysy">Rysy</a>, the highest peak of Poland, and the famous <a href="/wiki/Orla_Per%C4%87" title="Orla Perć">Orla Perć</a> mountain trail are located. The <a href="/wiki/Pieniny" title="Pieniny">Pieniny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bieszczady_Mountains" title="Bieszczady Mountains">Bieszczady Mountains</a> lie in the extreme south-east.<sup id="cite_ref-turism_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turism-149">[149]</a></sup> There are <a href="/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Poland" title="List of castles in Poland">over 100 castles</a> in the country, many in the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">Lower Silesian Voivodeship</a> and along the popular <a href="/wiki/Trail_of_the_Eagles%27_Nests" title="Trail of the Eagles' Nests">Trail of the Eagles' Nests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EaglesNests_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EaglesNests-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Poland" title="Energy in Poland">Energy in Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining_in_Poland" title="Coal mining in Poland">Coal mining in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg/220px-Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg/330px-Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg/440px-Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="509" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Elektrownia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Be%C5%82chat%C3%B3w_Power_Station" title="Bełchatów Power Station">Bełchatów Power Station</a> is a lignite-fired power station that produces 27–28 TWh of electricity per year, or 20% of the total power generation in Poland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The electricity generation sector in Poland is largely <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil-fuel</a>–based. Many power plants nationwide use Poland's position as a major European exporter of coal to their advantage by continuing to use coal as the primary raw material in production of their energy. In 2013, Poland scored 48 out of 129 states in the Energy Sustainability Index.<sup id="cite_ref-Energy_Sustainability_Index_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Sustainability_Index-151">[151]</a></sup> The three largest Polish coal mining firms (<a href="/wiki/W%C4%99glokoks" title="Węglokoks">Węglokoks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kompania_W%C4%99glowa" title="Kompania Węglowa">Kompania Węglowa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jastrz%C4%99bska_Sp%C3%B3%C5%82ka_W%C4%99glowa" title="Jastrzębska Spółka Węglowa">JSW</a>) extract around 100 million tonnes of coal annually. All three of these companies are key constituents of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a>'s lead economic indexes.</p>
<p>Renewable forms of energy account for a small<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (January 2014)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> proportion of Poland's full energy generation capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-EU_Commission_.E2.80.93_Energy_factsheet_P74_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU_Commission_.E2.80.93_Energy_factsheet_P74-152">[152]</a></sup> However, the national government has set targets for the development of renewable energy sources in Poland which should see the portion of power produced by renewable resources climb to 7.5% by 2010 and 15% by 2020. This is to be achieved mainly through the construction of <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farms</a> and a number of <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric">hydroelectric</a> stations.</p>
<p>Poland is thought to have<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (December 2016)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> around 164,800,000,000 m<sup>3</sup> of proven natural gas reserves and around 96,380,000 barrels of proven oil reserves. These reserves are exploited by energy supply companies such as <a href="/wiki/PKN_Orlen" title="PKN Orlen">PKN Orlen</a> ("the only Polish company listed in the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a>"). However, the small amounts of fossil fuels naturally occurring in Poland is insufficient to satisfy the full energy consumption needs of the population. Therefore, the country is a net importer of oil and natural gas.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Poland" title="Transport in Poland">Transport in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG/220px-Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG/330px-Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG/440px-Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wezelsosnicafromthesky.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/A1_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A1 autostrada (Poland)">A1</a>, <a href="/wiki/A4_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A4 autostrada (Poland)">A4</a> motorways and <a href="/wiki/National_roads_in_Poland" title="National roads in Poland">national road 44</a> junction near <a href="/wiki/Gliwice" title="Gliwice">Gliwice</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Transport in Poland is provided by means of <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Poland" title="Rail transport in Poland">rail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roads_and_expressways_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Roads and expressways in Poland">road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Merchant_Navy" title="Polish Merchant Navy">marine shipping</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Poland" title="List of airports in Poland">air travel.</a> Positioned in Central Europe with its eastern and part of its northeastern border constituting the longest land border of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> with the rest of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>.</p>
<p>Since joining the EU in May 2004, Poland has invested large amounts of public funds into modernization projects of its transport networks. The country now has a developing <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Poland" title="Highways in Poland">highways</a> network composed of motorways such as the <a href="/wiki/A1_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A1 autostrada (Poland)">A1</a>, <a href="/wiki/A2_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A2 autostrada (Poland)">A2</a>, <a href="/wiki/A4_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A4 autostrada (Poland)">A4</a>, <a href="/wiki/A8_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A8 autostrada (Poland)">A8</a>, <a href="/wiki/A18_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A18 autostrada (Poland)">A18</a> and express roads such as the <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S1_(Poland)" title="Expressway S1 (Poland)">S1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S3_(Poland)" title="Expressway S3 (Poland)">S3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S5_(Poland)" title="Expressway S5 (Poland)">S5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S7_(Poland)" title="Expressway S7 (Poland)">S7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S8_(Poland)" title="Expressway S8 (Poland)">S8</a>. At the end of 2016, Poland had 3163,4&#160;km of highways (1631,7&#160;km of motorways and 1531,7&#160;km of expressways). In addition to these newly built roads, many local and regional roads are being fixed as part of a national programme to rebuild all roads in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Road_Rebuilding_Program_.28Polish.29_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Road_Rebuilding_Program_.28Polish.29-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG/220px-Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG/330px-Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG/440px-Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_-_Pendolino.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/PKP_Intercity" title="PKP Intercity">PKP Intercity</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Pendolino" title="New Pendolino">Pendolino</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_railway_station" title="Wrocław Główny railway station">Wrocław Główny</a> railway station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2015, the nation had 11,800 miles (19,000&#160;km) of railway track. Trains can operate up to 99 miles per hour (159&#160;km/h) on 7.5% of the track. Most trains operate between 50 and 75 miles per hour (80 and 121&#160;km/h). Part of the system operates at 25 miles per hour (40&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Polish authorities maintain a program of improving operating speeds across the entire Polish rail network. Polish State Railways (PKP) are using new rolling stock such as Siemens Taurus ES64U4, which is in principle capable of speeds up to 200&#160;km/h (124&#160;mph). In December 2014, Poland began to implement <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Poland" title="High-speed rail in Poland">high–speed rail routes</a> connecting major Polish cities. The Polish government has revealed that it intends to connect all major cities to a future high-speed rail network by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-dec23_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dec23-155">[155]</a></sup> The new PKP Pendolino ETR 610 test train set the record for the fastest train in the history of Poland, reaching 293&#160;km/h (182&#160;mph) on 24 November 2013. Previously, the speed record had been 160&#160;km/h (99&#160;mph) since 1985. Most intercity rail routes in Poland are operated by <a href="/wiki/PKP_Intercity" title="PKP Intercity">PKP Intercity</a>, whilst regional trains are run by a number of operators, the largest of which is <a href="/wiki/Przewozy_Regionalne" title="Przewozy Regionalne">Przewozy Regionalne</a>.</p>
<p>On 14 December 2014, Polish State Railways started passenger service using the PKP Pendolino ED250, operating at 200&#160;km/h speed on 80&#160;km of line between Olszamowice and Zawiercie (part of the <a href="/wiki/PKP_rail_line_4" class="mw-redirect" title="PKP rail line 4">Central Rail Line</a> from Warsaw to Kraków). Currently, it is the line with highest railway speed in Poland.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg/220px-LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg/330px-LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg/440px-LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="814" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LOT_Boeing_787-8_SP-LRA_Lebeda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> is one of the world's oldest air carriers still in operation, originally established on 1 January 1929</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The air and maritime transport markets in Poland are largely well developed. Poland has a number of international airports, the largest of which is <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport">Warsaw Chopin Airport</a>, the primary global hub for <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a>. LOT is the 28th <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_airlines_in_Europe" title="List of largest airlines in Europe">largest European airline</a> and the world's 12th <a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_by_foundation_date" title="List of airlines by foundation date">oldest still in operation</a>, established in 1929 from a merger of <a href="/wiki/Aerolloyd" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerolloyd">Aerolloyd</a> (1922) and <a href="/wiki/Aero_(Polish_airline)" title="Aero (Polish airline)">Aero</a> (1925). Other major airports with international connections include <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_II_International_Airport_Krak%C3%B3w%E2%80%93Balice" title="John Paul II International Airport Kraków–Balice">John Paul II International Airport Kraków–Balice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw%E2%80%93Copernicus_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Wrocław–Copernicus Airport">Wrocław–Copernicus Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_Lech_Wa%C5%82%C4%99sa_Airport" title="Gdańsk Lech Wałęsa Airport">Gdańsk Lech Wałęsa Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84%E2%80%93%C5%81awica_Airport" title="Poznań–Ławica Airport">Poznań–Ławica Airport</a>.</p>
<p>Seaports exist all along Poland's Baltic coast, with most freight operations using <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Szczecin" title="Port of Szczecin">Szczecin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Port of Świnoujście">Świnoujście</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gdynia" title="Port of Gdynia">Gdynia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gda%C5%84sk" title="Port of Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Police" title="Port of Police">Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ko%C5%82obrzeg" title="Port of Kołobrzeg">Kołobrzeg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elbl%C4%85g" title="Elbląg">Elbląg</a> as their base. Passenger ferries link Poland with <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> all year round; these services are provided from Gdańsk and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Port of Świnoujście">Świnoujście</a> by <a href="/wiki/Polferries" title="Polferries">Polferries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stena_Line" title="Stena Line">Stena Line</a> from Gdynia and <a href="/wiki/Unity_Line" title="Unity Line">Unity Line</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie" title="Port of Świnoujście">Port of Świnoujście</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Polish_science_and_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish science and technology">Polish science and technology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palac-staszica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Palac-staszica.jpg/220px-Palac-staszica.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Palac-staszica.jpg/330px-Palac-staszica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Palac-staszica.jpg/440px-Palac-staszica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2356" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palac-staszica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Staszic_Palace" title="Staszic Palace">Staszic Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Polish Academy of Sciences">Polish Academy of Sciences</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland's tertiary education institutions; traditional <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Poland" title="List of universities in Poland">universities</a>, as well as technical, medical, and economic institutions, employ around 61,000 researchers and members of staff. There are around 300 research and development institutes, with about 10,000 researchers. In total, there are around 91,000 scientists in Poland today. However, in the 19th and 20th centuries many Polish scientists worked abroad; one of the most important of these exiles was <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sk%C5%82odowska-Curie" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Skłodowska-Curie">Maria Skłodowska-Curie</a>, a physicist and chemist who lived much of her life in France. In the first half of the 20th century, Poland was a flourishing centre of mathematics. Outstanding Polish mathematicians formed the <a href="/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w_School_of_Mathematics" title="Lwów School of Mathematics">Lwów School of Mathematics</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Banach" title="Stefan Banach">Stefan Banach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Mazur" title="Stanisław Mazur">Stanisław Mazur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Steinhaus" title="Hugo Steinhaus">Hugo Steinhaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Ulam" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanisław Ulam">Stanisław Ulam</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_School_of_Mathematics" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw School of Mathematics">Warsaw School of Mathematics</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Tarski" title="Alfred Tarski">Alfred Tarski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazimierz_Kuratowski" title="Kazimierz Kuratowski">Kazimierz Kuratowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wac%C5%82aw_Sierpi%C5%84ski" title="Wacław Sierpiński">Wacław Sierpiński</a>). The events of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> pushed many of them into exile. Such was the case of <a href="/wiki/Beno%C3%AEt_Mandelbrot" class="mw-redirect" title="Benoît Mandelbrot">Benoît Mandelbrot</a>, whose family left Poland when he was still a child. An alumnus of the Warsaw School of Mathematics was <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Zygmund" title="Antoni Zygmund">Antoni Zygmund</a>, one of the shapers of 20th century <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_analysis" title="Mathematical analysis">mathematical analysis</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marie_Curie_c1920.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Marie_Curie_c1920.png/150px-Marie_Curie_c1920.png" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Marie_Curie_c1920.png/225px-Marie_Curie_c1920.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Marie_Curie_c1920.png/300px-Marie_Curie_c1920.png 2x" data-file-width="453" data-file-height="679" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marie_Curie_c1920.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Physicist and chemist <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Maria Skłodowska-<br />
Curie</a>, the first person to win two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prizes</a>, established Poland's <a href="/wiki/Curie_Institute_(Warsaw)" class="mw-redirect" title="Curie Institute (Warsaw)">Radium Institute</a> in 1925<sup id="cite_ref-A_century_of_X-rays_and_radioactivity_in_medicine:_with_emphasis_on_photographic_records_of_the_early_years_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_century_of_X-rays_and_radioactivity_in_medicine:_with_emphasis_on_photographic_records_of_the_early_years-156">[156]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over 40 research and development centers and 4,500 researchers make Poland the biggest research and development hub in Central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chicagotribune1_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune1-158">[158]</a></sup> Multinational companies such as: ABB, <a href="/wiki/Delphi_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Delphi Corporation">Delphi</a>, <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett%E2%80%93Packard" class="mw-redirect" title="Hewlett–Packard">Hewlett–Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>, <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">LG Electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> all have set up research and development centres in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-159">[159]</a></sup> Companies chose Poland because of the availability of highly qualified labour force, presence of universities, support of authorities, and the largest market in East-Central Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-157">[157]</a></sup> According to a KPMG report in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-Why_Poland.3F_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Poland.3F-160">[160]</a></sup> 80% of Poland's current investors are content with their choice and willing to reinvest.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Poland" title="Telecommunications in Poland">Telecommunications in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg/170px-Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg/255px-Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg/340px-Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2832" data-file-height="4256" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budynek_TP_SA_w_Warszawie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> headquarters of the telecommunications provider <a href="/wiki/Orange_Polska" title="Orange Polska">Orange Polska</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The share of the telecom sector in the GDP was 4.4% (end of 2000 figure), compared to 2.5% in 1996. The coverage increased from 78 users per 1,000 inhabitants in 1989 to 282 in 2000. The value of the telecommunication market was zl 38.2bn (2006), and it grew by 12.4% in 2007 PMR.<sup id="cite_ref-Key_data_on_IT_and_telecoms_market_in_Poland.2C_2004.E2.80.932006_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Key_data_on_IT_and_telecoms_market_in_Poland.2C_2004.E2.80.932006-161">[161]</a></sup> The coverage mobile cellular was over 1000 users per 1000 people (2007). Telephones—mobile cellular: 38.7 million (Onet.pl&amp;GUS Report, 2007), telephones—main lines in use: 12.5 million (Telecom Team Report, 2005). In 2012, the process of converting to <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television" title="Digital terrestrial television">Digital terrestrial television</a> started, to be compatible with the rest of Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg/220px-Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg/330px-Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg/440px-Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1722" data-file-height="1359" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Poczta_gl_Bydgoszcz_4299.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main <a href="/wiki/Poczta_Polska" title="Poczta Polska">Post Office</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bydgoszcz" title="Bydgoszcz">Bydgoszcz</a>. Poland's postal service can trace its roots to the year 1558</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The public postal service in Poland is operated by <i><a href="/wiki/Poczta_Polska" title="Poczta Polska">Poczta Polska</a></i> (the Polish Post). It was created on 18 October 1558, when King <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus" title="Sigismund II Augustus">Sigismund II Augustus</a> established a permanent postal route from <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> to <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>. The service was dissolved during the foreign partitions. After regaining independence in 1918, Poland saw the rapid development of the postal system as new services were introduced including <a href="/wiki/Wire_transfer" title="Wire transfer">money transfers</a>, payment of pensions, delivery of magazines, and <a href="/wiki/Airmail" title="Airmail">air mail</a>.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Poland" title="List of wars involving Poland">wars and national uprisings</a> communication was provided mainly through the military authorities. Many important events in the history of Poland involved the postal service, like the <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_the_Polish_Post_Office_in_Danzig" class="mw-redirect" title="Defense of the Polish Post Office in Danzig">defence of the Polish Post Office in Gdańsk</a> in 1939, and the participation of the Polish Scouts' Postal Service in the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a>. Today,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the service is a modern state-owned company that provides a number of standard and express delivery as well as home-delivery services.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Poland" title="Demographics of Poland">Demographics of Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Poland" title="Demographic history of Poland">Demographic history of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:377px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_Poland.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Population_of_Poland.svg/375px-Population_of_Poland.svg.png" width="375" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Population_of_Poland.svg/563px-Population_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Population_of_Poland.svg/750px-Population_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="361" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_of_Poland.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population of Poland 1900–2010 in millions of inhabitants</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland, with 38,544,513 inhabitants, has the eighth-largest population in Europe and the sixth-largest in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. It has a population density of 122 inhabitants per square kilometer (328 per square mile).</p>
<p>Poland historically contained <a href="/wiki/Historical_demography_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical demography of Poland">many languages, cultures and religions</a> on its soil. The country had a particularly large Jewish population prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany's</a> regime led to the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Holocaust</a>. There were an estimated 3 million Jews living in Poland before the war—less than 300,000 survived. The outcome of the war, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland_after_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial changes of Poland after World War II">shift of Poland's borders</a> to the area between the <a href="/wiki/Curzon_Line" title="Curzon Line">Curzon Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oder-Neisse_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Oder-Neisse line">Oder-Neisse line</a>, coupled with post-war <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_evacuation_and_expulsion" title="World War II evacuation and expulsion">expulsion of minorities</a>, significantly reduced the country's ethnic diversity. Over 7 million <a href="/wiki/Emigration_from_Poland_to_Germany_after_World_War_II" title="Emigration from Poland to Germany after World War II">Germans fled or were expelled</a> from the Polish side of the Oder-Neisse boundary, after the country's borders were re-drawn by the big three Allied powers (United States, Britain and the Soviet Union) after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Langenbacher_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Langenbacher-162">[162]</a></sup> Post-World War II deportations were ordered by the Soviet authorities, who wished to remove the sizeable Polish minorities from Lithuania, Belarus and Ukraine and <a href="/wiki/Repatriation_of_Ukrainians_from_Poland_to_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Repatriation of Ukrainians from Poland to the Soviet Union">repatriation of Ukrainians from Poland to the Soviet Union</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial changes of Poland">territorial changes of Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Historical_demography_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical demography of Poland">historical demography of Poland</a> for details).</p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Polish_census_of_2002" title="Polish census of 2002">2002 census</a>, 36,983,700 people, or 96.74% of the population, consider themselves Polish, while 471,500 (1.23%) declared another nationality, and 774,900 (2.03%) did not declare any nationality. The largest minority nationalities and ethnic groups in Poland are <a href="/wiki/German_minority_in_Poland" title="German minority in Poland">Germans</a> (152,897 according to the census, 92% of whom live in <a href="/wiki/Opole_Voivodeship" title="Opole Voivodeship">Opole Voivodeship</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Silesian Voivodeship">Silesian Voivodeship</a>), <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> (c. 49,000), Ukrainians (c. 30,000), Lithuanians, Russians, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>, Jews, <a href="/wiki/Lemkos" title="Lemkos">Lemkos</a>, Slovaks, Czechs, and <a href="/wiki/Lipka_Tatars" title="Lipka Tatars">Lipka Tatars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tolerance_and_Cultural_Diversity_Discourses_in_Poland_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tolerance_and_Cultural_Diversity_Discourses_in_Poland-163">[163]</a></sup> Among foreign citizens, the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a> are the largest ethnic group, followed by Armenians and Greeks.</p>
<p>The Polish language, part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic languages</a>, functions as the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Poland. Until recent decades Russian was commonly learned as a second language, but has been replaced by English as the most common second language studied and spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-Poles_return_to_Russian_language_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poles_return_to_Russian_language-164">[164]</a></sup> In 2015, more than 50% of Poles declared to speak English – Russian came second and German came third, other commonly spoken languages include French, Italian and Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>In recent years, Poland's population has decreased due to an increase in emigration and a decline in the birth rate. Since Poland's accession to the European Union, a significant number of Poles <a href="/wiki/Migrations_from_Poland_since_EU_accession" title="Migrations from Poland since EU accession">have emigrated</a>, primarily to the <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Poles in the United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_Germany" title="Poles in Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polish_minority_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Polish minority in the Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> in search of better work opportunities abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-onet_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onet-166">[166]</a></sup> With better economic conditions and Polish salaries at 70% of the EU average in 2016, this trend started to decrease in the 2010s and workforce became needed in the country. As a result, the Polish Minister of Development <a href="/wiki/Mateusz_Morawiecki" title="Mateusz Morawiecki">Mateusz Morawiecki</a> suggested that Poles abroad should return to Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Polish minorities are still present in the neighboring countries of Ukraine, Belarus, and Lithuania, as well as in other countries (see <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> for population numbers). Altogether, the number of ethnic Poles living abroad is estimated to be around 20&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-Polish_Diaspora_.28Polonia.29_Worldwide_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polish_Diaspora_.28Polonia.29_Worldwide-168">[168]</a></sup> The largest number of <a href="/wiki/Polish_diaspora" title="Polish diaspora">Poles outside of Poland</a> can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish American">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_Germany" title="Poles in Germany">Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Centers_of_Polish_Immigration_in_the_World_.E2.80.93_USA_and_Germany_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centers_of_Polish_Immigration_in_the_World_.E2.80.93_USA_and_Germany-169">[169]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) in Poland was estimated in 2013 at 1.33 children born to a woman.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Poland" title="Languages of Poland">Languages of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg/220px-Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg/330px-Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg/440px-Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2778" data-file-height="1461" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolina_Jadwigi_znak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Dolina Jadwigi</i>—a <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a> (Polish-Kashubian) road sign with the village name</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Polish</b> (<i>język polski</i>, <i>polszczyzna</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic language</a> spoken primarily in Poland and the <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">native language</a> of Poles. It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Lechitic_languages" title="Lechitic languages">Lechitic</a> subgroup of <a href="/wiki/West_Slavic_languages" title="West Slavic languages">West Slavic languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Polish is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Poland, but it is also used throughout the world by <a href="/wiki/Polish_diaspora" title="Polish diaspora">Polish minorities</a> in other countries. It is one of the official <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_European_Union" title="Languages of the European Union">languages of the European Union</a>. Its written standard is the <a href="/wiki/Polish_alphabet" title="Polish alphabet">Polish alphabet</a>, which has 9 additions to the letters of the basic <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> (<i>ą</i>, <i>ć</i>, <i>ę</i>, <i>ł</i>, <i>ń</i>, <i>ó</i>, <i>ś</i>, <i>ź</i>, <i>ż</i>). The deaf communities use <a href="/wiki/Polish_Sign_Language" title="Polish Sign Language">Polish Sign Language</a> belonging to the <a href="/wiki/German_Sign_Language" title="German Sign Language">German family of Sign Languages</a>.</p>
<p>According to the <i>Act of 6 January 2005 on national and ethnic minorities and on the regional languages</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> 16 other languages have officially recognized status of minority languages: 1 regional language, 10 languages of 9 national minorities (minority groups that have their own independent state elsewhere) and 5 languages of 4 ethnic minorities spoken by the members of minorities not having a separate state elsewhere). Jewish and Romani minorities each have 2 minority languages recognized.</p>
<p>Languages having the status of national minority's language are Armenian, Belarusian, Czech, German, Yiddish, Hebrew, Lithuanian, Russian, Slovak and Ukrainian. Languages having the status of ethnic minority's language are <a href="/wiki/Karaim_language" title="Karaim language">Karaim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashubian_language" title="Kashubian language">Kashubian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">Rusyn</a> (called <i>Lemko</i> in Poland) and <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a>. Also, official recognition is granted to two <a href="/wiki/Romani_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Romani languages">Romani languages</a>: <a href="/wiki/Polska_Roma" title="Polska Roma">Polska Roma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bergitka_Roma" title="Bergitka Roma">Bergitka Roma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>Official recognition of a language provides certain rights (under conditions prescribed by the law): of education in that language, of having the language established as the secondary administrative language or help language in bilingual <a href="/wiki/Bilingual_communes_in_Poland" title="Bilingual communes in Poland">municipalities</a> and of financial support from the state for the promotion of that language.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Poland" title="Religion in Poland">Religion in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkCyan; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religions (1%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG/220px-Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG/330px-Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG/440px-Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cz%C4%99stochowa_-_Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_AL04.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_Monastery" title="Jasna Góra Monastery">Jasna Góra Monastery</a> is a major pilgrimage site for Poland's many Catholics</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From its beginnings, Poland has contributed substantially to the development of religious freedom. Since the country adopted Christianity in 966, it was also welcoming to other religions through a series of laws: <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Kalisz" title="Statute of Kalisz">Statute of Kalisz</a> (1264), <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Confederation" title="Warsaw Confederation">Warsaw Confederation</a> (1573). The Polish king <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Władysław II Jagiełło">Władysław II Jagiełło</a>, however, was pressed by the Catholic Church to issue the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Wielu%C5%84" title="Edict of Wieluń">Edict of Wieluń</a> (1424), outlawing early Protestant <a href="/wiki/Hussite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussite">Hussitism</a>. Polish theological thought includes movements such as Calvinist <a href="/wiki/Polish_Brethren" title="Polish Brethren">Polish Brethren</a> and a number of other Protestant groups, as well as atheists, such as ex-Jesuit philosopher <a href="/wiki/Kazimierz_%C5%81yszczy%C5%84ski" title="Kazimierz Łyszczyński">Kazimierz Łyszczyński</a>, one of the first atheist thinkers in Europe. Also, in the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Anabaptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anabaptist">Anabaptists</a> from the Netherlands and Germany settled in Poland—after being persecuted in Western Europe—and became known as the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_delta_Mennonites" title="Vistula delta Mennonites">Vistula delta Mennonites</a>.</p>
<p>Until World War II Poland was a religiously diverse society, in which substantial <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Christian Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Christian</a> and Roman Catholic groups coexisted.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> In the Second Polish Republic, Roman Catholic was the dominant religion, declared by about 65% of the Polish citizens, followed by other Christian denominations, and about 3% of Judaism believers.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> and the post–World War II <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_from_Poland_during_and_after_World_War_II" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans from Poland during and after World War II">flight and expulsion of German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Vistula" title="Operation Vistula">Ukrainian</a> populations, Poland has become overwhelmingly Roman Catholic. In 2007, 88.4% of the population belonged to the Catholic Church.<sup id="cite_ref-Maly_Rocznik_Statystyczny_Polski_2009_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maly_Rocznik_Statystyczny_Polski_2009-176">[176]</a></sup> Though rates of religious observance are lower, at 52%<sup id="cite_ref-ekumenizm_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ekumenizm-177">[177]</a></sup> or 51% of the Polish Catholics,<sup id="cite_ref-archive9_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive9-178">[178]</a></sup> Poland remains one of the most devoutly religious countries in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-cbos_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbos-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 16 October 1978 until his death on 2 April 2005, <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_II" class="mw-redirect" title="John Paul II">Karol Józef Wojtyła</a> reigned as <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Supreme Pontiff</a> of the Roman Catholic Church. He is the only Polish Pope to date.<sup id="cite_ref-About_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-180">[180]</a></sup> Additionally he is credited with having played a significant role in hastening the downfall of communism in Poland and throughout <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom.C3.ADnguez_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom.C3.ADnguez-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Communism_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Communism-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg/220px-Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg/330px-Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg/440px-Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2996" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerkiew_w_Turza%C5%84sku.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._Michael_Archangel%27s_Church,_Turza%C5%84sk" title="St. Michael Archangel's Church, Turzańsk">St. Michael Archangel's Tserkva</a>, an Orthodox Church in the <a href="/wiki/Wooden_tserkvas_of_the_Carpathian_region_in_Poland_and_Ukraine" title="Wooden tserkvas of the Carpathian region in Poland and Ukraine">Carpathian region of Poland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Religious minorities include <a href="/wiki/Polish_Orthodox_Church" title="Polish Orthodox Church">Polish Orthodox</a> (about 506,800),<sup id="cite_ref-CSO_2008_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSO_2008-8">[8]</a></sup> various Protestants (about 150,000),<sup id="cite_ref-CSO_2008_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSO_2008-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (126,827),<sup id="cite_ref-CSO_2008_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSO_2008-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariavite_Church" title="Mariavite Church">Mariavites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_National_Catholic_Church" title="Polish National Catholic Church">Polish Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">Jews</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Poland" title="Islam in Poland">Muslims</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82ystok" title="Białystok">Białystok</a>). Members of Protestant churches include about 77,500 <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a> in the largest <a href="/wiki/Evangelical-Augsburg_Church_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical-Augsburg Church in Poland">Evangelical-Augsburg Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CSO_2008_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSO_2008-8">[8]</a></sup> 23,000 <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal_Church_in_Poland" title="Pentecostal Church in Poland">Pentecostal Church in Poland</a>, and smaller numbers in various <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestant</a> churches. There are also a several thousand neopagans, some of whom are members of officially registered churches such as the <a href="/wiki/Native_Polish_Church" title="Native Polish Church">Native Polish Church</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg/220px-Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg/330px-Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg/440px-Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Krakow_Synagoga_Tempel_20071111_1123_2077.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kraków's <a href="/wiki/Tempel_Synagogue,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Tempel Synagogue, Kraków">Tempel Synagogue</a> is one of the largest in Poland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Freedom of religion is now guaranteed by the 1989 statute of the Polish Constitution,<sup id="cite_ref-Wyznania_religijne_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wyznania_religijne-183">[183]</a></sup> enabling the emergence of additional denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-www10_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www10-184">[184]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Concordat" title="Concordat">Concordat</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> and Poland guarantees the teaching of religion in state<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> schools. According to a 2007 survey, 72% of respondents were not opposed to <a href="/wiki/Catechism" title="Catechism">religious instruction</a> in public schools; alternative courses in ethics are available only in one percent of the entire public educational system.<sup id="cite_ref-gazeta11_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gazeta11-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>Famous sites of Roman Catholic pilgrimage in Poland include the <a href="/wiki/Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_Monastery" title="Jasna Góra Monastery">Monastery of Jasna Góra</a> in the southern Polish city of <a href="/wiki/Cz%C4%99stochowa" title="Częstochowa">Częstochowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Liche%C5%84" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Licheń">Basilica of Our Lady of Licheń</a>, <a href="/wiki/Divine_Mercy_Sanctuary,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Divine Mercy Sanctuary, Kraków">Divine Mercy Sanctuary, Kraków</a>. Many tourists also visit the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Father_John_Paul_II_Family_Home_in_Wadowice" title="Holy Father John Paul II Family Home in Wadowice">Family home of John Paul II</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wadowice" title="Wadowice">Wadowice</a> just outside <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>. Orthodox pilgrims visit Mountain Grabarka near <a href="/wiki/Grabarka-Klasztor" title="Grabarka-Klasztor">Grabarka-Klasztor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Health in Poland">Health in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg/170px-Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg/255px-Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg/340px-Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="504" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uniwersytecki_Szpital_Kliniczny_Gdansk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_Medical_University" title="Gdańsk Medical University">University Medical Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland's healthcare system is based on an all-inclusive insurance system. State subsidised healthcare is available to all Polish citizens who are covered by this general health insurance program. However, it is not compulsory to be treated in a state-run hospital as a number of private medical complexes exist nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-justlanded_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justlanded-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>All medical service providers and hospitals in Poland are subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Health of the Republic of Poland">Polish Ministry of Health</a>, which provides oversight and scrutiny of general medical practice as well as being responsible for the day-to-day administration of the healthcare system. In addition to these roles, the ministry is tasked with the maintenance of standards of hygiene and patient-care.</p>
<p>Hospitals in Poland are organised according to the regional administrative structure, resultantly most towns have their own hospital <i>(Szpital Miejski)</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Larger and more specialised medical complexes tend only to be found in larger cities, with some even more specialised units located only in the capital, Warsaw. However, all <a href="/wiki/Voivodeship" title="Voivodeship">voivodeships</a> have their own general hospital (most have more than one), all of which are obliged to have a trauma centre; these types of hospital, which are able to deal with almost all medical problems are called 'regional hospitals' <i>(Szpital Wojewódzki)</i>. The last category of hospital in Poland is that of specialised medical centres, an example of which would be the <a href="/wiki/Curie_Institute,_Warsaw" title="Curie Institute, Warsaw">Skłodowska-Curie Institute of Oncology</a>, Poland's leading, and most highly specialised centre for the research and treatment of cancer.</p>
<p>In 2012, the Polish health-care industry experienced a transformation. Hospitals were given priority for refurbishment where necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-Polish_hospitals_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polish_hospitals-189">[189]</a></sup> As a result of this process, many hospitals were updated with the latest medical equipment.</p>
<p>In 2013, the average life expectancy at birth was 76.45 years (72.53 years infant male/80.62 years infant female).<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Poland" title="Education in Poland">Education in Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universities_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Universities in Poland">Universities in Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Poland" title="List of schools in Poland">List of schools in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_%284%29.jpg/220px-Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_%284%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_%284%29.jpg/330px-Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_%284%29.jpg/440px-Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="466" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryszard_Kaczorowski_21_02_2008_(4).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wearing of traditional <a href="/wiki/Academic_dress" title="Academic dress">academic regalia</a> is a common feature of Polish university ceremonies</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PL-uczelnie.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/PL-uczelnie.png/220px-PL-uczelnie.png" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/PL-uczelnie.png/330px-PL-uczelnie.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/PL-uczelnie.png/440px-PL-uczelnie.png 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1467" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PL-uczelnie.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Density of collegiate-level institutions of higher education</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Commission_of_National_Education" title="Commission of National Education">Commission of National Education</a> (<i>Komisja Edukacji Narodowej</i>) established in 1773, was the world's first state ministry of education.<sup id="cite_ref-Meer2002-223_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meer2002-223-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Davies2005_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2005-192">[192]</a></sup> The education of Polish society was a goal of the nation's rulers as early as the 12th century. The library catalogue of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_chapter" title="Cathedral chapter">Cathedral Chapter</a> of Kraków dating back to 1110 shows that in the early 12th-century Polish academia had access to European and Classical literature. The <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a> was founded in 1364 by <a href="/wiki/Casimir_III_the_Great" title="Casimir III the Great">King Casimir III</a> in Kraków—the school is <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest universities in continuous operation">the world's 19th oldest university</a>.</p>
<p>The modern-day <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a>, coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a>, ranks Poland's educational system in its <a href="/wiki/PISA_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="PISA 2012">PISA 2012</a> as the 10th best in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> scoring higher than the OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>Education in Poland starts at the age of five or six (with the particular age chosen by the parents) for the '0' class (Kindergarten) and six or seven years in the 1st class of primary school (Polish <i>szkoła podstawowa</i>). It is compulsory that children participate in one year of formal education before entering the 1st class at no later than 7 years of age. Corporal punishment of children in schools is officially prohibited since 1783 (before the partitions) and criminalised since 2010 (in schools as well as at home).</p>
<p>At the end of the 6th class when students are 13, students take a compulsory exam that will determine their acceptance and transition into a specific lower secondary school (<i>gimnazjum, pronounced gheem-nah-sium</i>) (Middle School/Junior High). They will attend this school for three years during classes 7, 8, and 9. Students then take another compulsory exam to determine the upper secondary level school they will attend. There are several alternatives, the most common being the three years in a <i>liceum</i> or four years in a <a href="/wiki/Technikum" class="mw-redirect" title="Technikum">technikum</a>. Both end with a maturity examination (<a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">matura</a>—similar to French <a href="/wiki/Baccalaur%C3%A9at" title="Baccalauréat">baccalauréat</a>), and may be followed by several forms of higher education, leading to <a href="/wiki/Licencjat" class="mw-redirect" title="Licencjat">licencjat</a> or inżynier (the Polish <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a> first cycle qualification), <a href="/wiki/Magister_(degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magister (degree)">magister</a> (second cycle qualification) and eventually <a href="/wiki/Doktor" class="mw-redirect" title="Doktor">doktor</a> (third cycle qualification).<sup id="cite_ref-The_impact_of_the_1999_education_reform_in_Poland_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_impact_of_the_1999_education_reform_in_Poland-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Poland, there are 500 university-level institutions for the pursuit of higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-GUS-2_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GUS-2-196">[196]</a></sup> There are 18 fully accredited traditional universities, 20 technical universities, 9 independent medical universities, 5 universities for the study of economics, 9 agricultural academies, 3 pedagogical universities, a theological academy, 3 maritime service universities and 4 national military academies. Also, there are a number of higher educational institutions dedicated to the teaching of the arts—amongst these are the 7 academies of music.</p>
