</center>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Poland" title="Culture of Poland">Culture of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg/170px-Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg" width="170" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg/255px-Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg/340px-Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg 2x" data-file-width="491" data-file-height="650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schweikart_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko" title="Tadeusz Kościuszko">Tadeusz Kościuszko</a> was a veteran and hero of both <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Russian_War_of_1792" title="Polish–Russian War of 1792">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American</a> wars of independence between 1765 and 1794<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The culture of Poland is closely connected with its intricate 1,000-year <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland" title="History of Poland">history</a><sup id="cite_ref-amazon_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amazon-199">[199]</a></sup> Its unique character developed as a result of its geography at the confluence of European cultures. With origins in the culture of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavs" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Slavs">Proto-Slavs</a>, over time Polish culture has been profoundly influenced by its interweaving ties with the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Latinate">Latinate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> worlds as well as in continual dialog with the many other ethnic groups and minorities living in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA-200">[200]</a></sup> The people of Poland have traditionally been seen as hospitable to artists from abroad and eager to follow cultural and artistic trends popular in other countries. In the 19th and 20th centuries the Polish focus on cultural advancement often took precedence over political and economic activity. These factors have contributed to the versatile nature of Polish art, with all its complex nuances.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_people">Famous people</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg/170px-Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg/255px-Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg/340px-Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="556" data-file-height="648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nikolaus_Kopernikus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Nicolaus Copernicus</a>, the 16th-century Polish astronomer who formulated the <a href="/wiki/Heliocentrism" title="Heliocentrism">heliocentric</a> model of the solar system that placed the Sun rather than the Earth at its center—work first published in 1543</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_people" title="List of Polish people">list of famous Poles</a> begins in earnest with the polymath <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Mikołaj Kopernik</a> (Nicolaus Copernicus),<sup id="cite_ref-copernicus_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-copernicus-201">[201]</a></sup> who studied at the <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a> founded in 1364 by Casimir the Great from proceeds of his <a href="/wiki/Wieliczka_Salt_Mine" title="Wieliczka Salt Mine">Wieliczka Salt Mine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> Poland is the birthplace of many distinguished personalities among whom are: <a href="/wiki/Fryderyk_Chopin" class="mw-redirect" title="Fryderyk Chopin">Fryderyk Chopin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Le_petit_Robert_2_:_.28dictionnaire_universel_des_noms_propres.2C_alphab.C3.A9tique_et_analogique_.29_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le_petit_Robert_2_:_.28dictionnaire_universel_des_noms_propres.2C_alphab.C3.A9tique_et_analogique_.29-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Concise_Oxford_dictionary_of_music_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Concise_Oxford_dictionary_of_music-204">[204]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sk%C5%82odowska_Curie" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Skłodowska Curie">Maria Skłodowska Curie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Maria_Sklodowska._La_jeunesse_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maria_Sklodowska._La_jeunesse-205">[205]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko" title="Tadeusz Kościuszko">Tadeusz Kościuszko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazimierz_Pu%C5%82aski" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazimierz Pułaski">Kazimierz Pułaski</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski" title="Józef Piłsudski">Józef Piłsudski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lech_Wa%C5%82%C4%99sa" title="Lech Wałęsa">Lech Wałęsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> (Karol Wojtyła). Great Polish painter <a href="/wiki/Jan_Matejko" title="Jan Matejko">Jan Matejko</a> devoted his monumental art to the most significant historical events on Polish lands, along with the playwright, painter and poet <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Wyspia%C5%84ski" title="Stanisław Wyspiański">Stanisław Wyspiański</a>. <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Ignacy_Witkiewicz" title="Stanisław Ignacy Witkiewicz">Stanisław Ignacy Witkiewicz (Witkacy)</a> was an example of a Polish avant-garde philosopher and author of aesthetic theories. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Conrad" title="Joseph Conrad">Joseph Conrad</a> was a notable author of works in English.<sup id="cite_ref-Profiles_.E2.80.93_Joseph_Conrad_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profiles_.E2.80.93_Joseph_Conrad-206">[206]</a></sup> Many world-famous <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Poland" title="Cinema of Poland">Polish movie directors</a> include <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polański</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Wajda" title="Andrzej Wajda">Andrzej Wajda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zbigniew_Rybczy%C5%84ski" title="Zbigniew Rybczyński">Zbigniew Rybczyński</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janusz_Kami%C5%84ski" title="Janusz Kamiński">Janusz Kamiński</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Kie%C5%9Blowski" title="Krzysztof Kieślowski">Krzysztof Kieślowski</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Holland" title="Agnieszka Holland">Agnieszka Holland</a>. Actresses known outside of Poland, include <a href="/wiki/Helena_Modjeska" title="Helena Modjeska">Helena Modjeska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pola_Negri" title="Pola Negri">Pola Negri</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span></h3>
<p>Poland has maintained a high level of <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, an established <a href="/wiki/Disability_rights_movement" title="Disability rights movement">disability rights movement</a> and promotes peaceful equality.<sup id="cite_ref-ND2005_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ND2005-207">[207]</a></sup> Unlike in many other countries, ethnic <a href="/wiki/Minority_rights" title="Minority rights">minority rights</a> in Poland are guaranteed directly by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Poland" title="Constitution of Poland">Constitution of Poland</a> (art. 35).<sup id="cite_ref-minelres_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minelres-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG/170px-John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG/255px-John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG 2x" data-file-width="276" data-file-height="360" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Paul_II_1980_cropped.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">John Paul II</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Pole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slav</a> to become a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> Pope. He held the papacy between 1978 and 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout most of its history, Poland has experienced only very limited immigration from abroad; this trend can be largely attributed to Poland's rejection of slavery and to a lack of overseas colonies as well as occupation of its territories during much of the 19th and early 20th centuries. Despite this, the country has for a long time been regarded as having a very tolerant society, which affords equal rights to all people no matter what their ethnic background.<sup id="cite_ref-ND2005_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ND2005-207">[207]</a></sup> This can be said to stem largely from the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Casimir_III_the_Great" title="Casimir III the Great">Casimir III the Great</a> and his acceptance of Poland's <a href="/wiki/Jewish_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish community">Jewish community</a>, in a time when most of Europe recessed into <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic">antisemitic</a> moods and actions. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jews_in_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Jews in Poland">history of Jews in Poland</a> exemplifies peaceful co-existence of a nation with a particular ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-ND2005_207-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ND2005-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">Polish parliament</a> rejected <a href="/wiki/Recognition_of_same-sex_unions_in_Poland#Legislation" title="Recognition of same-sex unions in Poland">proposed legislation</a> for civil partnerships, which the majority of Polish society is against,<sup id="cite_ref-CBOS_Civil_union_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBOS_Civil_union-209">[209]</a></sup> but for the first time it gave an asylum to a gay person from Uganda on the basis of the sexual orientation.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> In a 2013 opinion poll conducted by <a href="/wiki/Centrum_Badania_Opinii_Spo%C5%82ecznej" class="mw-redirect" title="Centrum Badania Opinii Społecznej">CBOS</a>, 60% of Poles were against homosexual civil partnerships, 72% were against <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>, 88% were against adoption by same-sex couples, and 68% were against gays and lesbians publicly showing their way of life.<sup id="cite_ref-CBOS_Civil_union_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBOS_Civil_union-209">[209]</a></sup> Article 18 of the Constitution of Poland bans same-sex marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Poland" title="Music of Poland">Music of Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg/170px-Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg/255px-Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg/340px-Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1014" data-file-height="1455" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Fryderyk Chopin</a> was a renowned classical composer and virtuoso pianist.</div>
</div>
</div>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div style="background:transparent;text-align:left;padding:2px"><b><a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Frédéric Chopin</a></b></div>
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Frederic_Chopin_-_mazurka_no._4_in_a_minor,_op._17.ogg" title="File:Frederic Chopin - mazurka no. 4 in a minor, op. 17.ogg">Mazurka no. 4 in a minor, op. 17</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="334.95616780045" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Frederic_Chopin_-_mazurka_no._4_in_a_minor,_op._17.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons">
<source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ca/Frederic_Chopin_-_mazurka_no._4_in_a_minor%2C_op._17.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (153 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="152769" /></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"><a href="/wiki/Mazurka" title="Mazurka">Mazurka</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <span lang="pl"><i>mazurek</i></span>), stylized <a href="/wiki/Folk_dance" title="Folk dance">folk dance</a> in <a href="/wiki/Triple_meter" class="mw-redirect" title="Triple meter">triple meter</a> (1832), commemorating the <a href="/wiki/November_Uprising" title="November Uprising">November Uprising</a></div>
</div>
<hr /></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Artists from Poland, including famous composers like <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Chopin</a> or <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Penderecki" title="Krzysztof Penderecki">Penderecki</a> and traditional, regionalized <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk musicians</a>, create a lively and diverse music scene, which even recognizes its own music genres, such as <a href="/wiki/Poezja_%C5%9Bpiewana" class="mw-redirect" title="Poezja śpiewana">poezja śpiewana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disco_polo" title="Disco polo">disco polo</a>. As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Poland&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Poland is one of the few countries in Europe where <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> dominate over pop music, while all kinds of <a href="/wiki/Alternative_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative music">alternative music</a> genres are encouraged.<sup id="cite_ref-Khan.2FMetz_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khan.2FMetz-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>The origins of Polish music can be traced as far back as the 13th century; manuscripts have been found in <a href="/wiki/Stary_S%C4%85cz" title="Stary Sącz">Stary Sącz</a>, containing <a href="/wiki/Polyphony" title="Polyphony">polyphonic</a> compositions related to the Parisian <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Notre Dame School">Notre Dame School</a>. Other early compositions, such as the melody of <i><a href="/wiki/Bogurodzica" title="Bogurodzica">Bogurodzica</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/B%C3%B3g_si%C4%99_rodzi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bóg się rodzi">Bóg się rodzi</a></i> (a coronation polonaise for Polish kings by an unknown composer), may also date back to this period, however, the first known notable composer, <a href="/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_z_Radomia" title="Mikołaj z Radomia">Mikołaj z Radomia</a>, was born and lived in the 15th century. During the 16th century, two main musical groups – both based in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> and belonging to the King and Archbishop of Wawel – led to the rapid development of Polish music. Composers writing during this period include <a href="/wiki/Wac%C5%82aw_z_Szamotu%C5%82" class="mw-redirect" title="Wacław z Szamotuł">Wacław z Szamotuł</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_Ziele%C5%84ski" title="Mikołaj Zieleński">Mikołaj Zieleński</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_Gom%C3%B3%C5%82ka" title="Mikołaj Gomółka">Mikołaj Gomółka</a>. <a href="/wiki/Diomedes_Cato" title="Diomedes Cato">Diomedes Cato</a>, a native-born Italian who lived in Kraków from about the age of five, became a renowned lutenist at the court of Sigismund III, and not only imported some of the musical styles from southern Europe, but blended them with native folk music.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Music_Courts_of_the_Polish_Vasas_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Music_Courts_of_the_Polish_Vasas-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg/170px-Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg/255px-Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg/340px-Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Rubinstein_1962.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rubinstein" title="Arthur Rubinstein">Artur Rubinstein</a> was one of the greatest concert pianists of the 20th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of the 18th century, Polish classical music evolved into national forms like the <a href="/wiki/Polonaise" title="Polonaise">polonaise</a>. In the 19th century the most popular composers were: <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Elsner" title="Józef Elsner">Józef Elsner</a> and his pupils <a href="/wiki/Fryderyk_Chopin" class="mw-redirect" title="Fryderyk Chopin">Fryderyk Chopin</a> and Ignacy Dobrzyński. Important opera composers of the era were <a href="/wiki/Karol_Kurpi%C5%84ski" title="Karol Kurpiński">Karol Kurpiński</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Moniuszko" title="Stanisław Moniuszko">Stanisław Moniuszko</a> whilst the list of famous soloists and composers included <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Wieniawski" title="Henryk Wieniawski">Henryk Wieniawski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juliusz_Zar%C4%99bski" title="Juliusz Zarębski">Juliusz Zarębski</a>. At the turn of the 19th and 20th centuries the most prominent composers could said to have been <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_%C5%BBele%C5%84ski_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Władysław Żeleński (musician)">Władysław Zeleński</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mieczys%C5%82aw_Kar%C5%82owicz" title="Mieczysław Karłowicz">Mieczysław Karłowicz</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Karol_Szymanowski" title="Karol Szymanowski">Karol Szymanowski</a> gaining prominence prior to World War II. <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Tansman" title="Alexandre Tansman">Alexandre Tansman</a> lived in Paris but had strong connections with Poland. <a href="/wiki/Witold_Lutos%C5%82awski" title="Witold Lutosławski">Witold Lutosławski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henryk_G%C3%B3recki" title="Henryk Górecki">Henryk Górecki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Penderecki" title="Krzysztof Penderecki">Krzysztof Penderecki</a> composed in Poland, <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Panufnik" title="Andrzej Panufnik">Andrzej Panufnik</a> emigrated.</p>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small-left" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div style="background:transparent;text-align:left;padding:2px"><b><a href="/wiki/Ballades_(Chopin)" title="Ballades (Chopin)">Ballade form</a> invented by <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Chopin</a></b>.<sup id="cite_ref-chopinmusic.net-ballades_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chopinmusic.net-ballades-214">[214]</a></sup></div>
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Frederic_Chopin_-_ballade_no._3_in_a_flat_major,_op._47.ogg" title="File:Frederic Chopin - ballade no. 3 in a flat major, op. 47.ogg">Ballade no. 3 in a-flat major, op. 47</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_2" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="557.04922902494" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Frederic_Chopin_-_ballade_no._3_in_a_flat_major,_op._47.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons">
<source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c8/Frederic_Chopin_-_ballade_no._3_in_a_flat_major%2C_op._47.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (147 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="147307" /></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Inspired by poems of <a href="/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz" title="Adam Mickiewicz">Adam Mickiewicz</a></div>
</div>
<hr /></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Traditional Polish folk music has had a major effect on the works of many well-known Polish composers, and no more so than on Fryderyk Chopin, a widely recognised national hero of the arts. All of Chopin's <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" class="mw-redirect" title="List of compositions by Frédéric Chopin">works</a> involve the piano and are technically demanding, emphasising nuance and expressive depth. As a great composer, Chopin invented the <a href="/wiki/Musical_form" title="Musical form">musical form</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Ballade_(classical_music)#Instrumental_ballades" title="Ballade (classical music)">instrumental ballade</a> and made major innovations to the <a href="/wiki/Piano_sonata" title="Piano sonata">piano sonata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazurka" title="Mazurka">mazurka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">waltz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nocturne" title="Nocturne">nocturne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polonaise" title="Polonaise">polonaise</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tude" title="Étude">étude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Impromptu" title="Impromptu">impromptu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prelude_(music)" title="Prelude (music)">prélude</a>, he was also the composer of a number of polonaises which borrowed heavily from traditional Polish folk music. It is largely thanks to him that the such pieces gained great popularity throughout Europe during the 19th century. Nowadays the most distinctive folk music can be heard in the towns and villages of the mountainous south, particularly in the region surrounding the winter resort town of <a href="/wiki/Zakopane" title="Zakopane">Zakopane</a>.</p>
<p>Today Poland has a very active music scene, with the jazz and metal genres being particularly popular among the contemporary populace. Polish jazz musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Komeda" title="Krzysztof Komeda">Krzysztof Komeda</a>, created a unique style, which was most famous in the 1960s and 1970s and continues to be popular to this day. Since the fall of Communism, Poland has become a major venue for large-scale music festivals, chief among which are the <a href="/wiki/Open%27er_Festival" title="Open'er Festival">Open'er Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opole_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Opole Festival">Opole Festival</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sopot_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Sopot Festival">Sopot Festival</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_artists" title="List of Polish artists">List of Polish artists</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prussian_Homage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Prussian_Homage.jpg/400px-Prussian_Homage.jpg" width="400" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Prussian_Homage.jpg/600px-Prussian_Homage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Prussian_Homage.jpg/800px-Prussian_Homage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1183" data-file-height="575" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prussian_Homage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prussian_Homage_(painting)" title="Prussian Homage (painting)"><i>Prussian Homage</i></a> (<i>Hołd pruski</i>), painted by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Matejko" title="Jan Matejko">Jan Matejko</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Polish art has always reflected European trends while maintaining its unique character. The <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> school of Historicist painting developed by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Matejko" title="Jan Matejko">Jan Matejko</a> produced monumental portrayals of customs and significant events in Polish history. <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Witkiewicz" title="Stanisław Witkiewicz">Stanisław Witkiewicz</a> was an ardent supporter of <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">realism</a> in Polish art, its main representative being <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Marian_Che%C5%82mo%C5%84ski" class="mw-redirect" title="Józef Marian Chełmoński">Jozef Chełmoński</a>. The Młoda Polska (<a href="/wiki/Young_Poland" title="Young Poland">Young Poland</a>) movement witnessed the birth of modern Polish art, and engaged in a great deal of formal experimentation led by <a href="/wiki/Jacek_Malczewski" title="Jacek Malczewski">Jacek Malczewski</a> (<a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">Symbolism</a>), <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Wyspia%C5%84ski" title="Stanisław Wyspiański">Stanisław Wyspiański</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Mehoffer" title="Józef Mehoffer">Józef Mehoffer</a>, and a group of Polish <a href="/wiki/Impressionists" class="mw-redirect" title="Impressionists">Impressionists</a>. Artists of the twentieth-century Avant-Garde represented various schools and trends. The art of <a href="/wiki/Tadeusz_Makowski" title="Tadeusz Makowski">Tadeusz Makowski</a> was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">Cubism</a>; while <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Strzemi%C5%84ski" title="Władysław Strzemiński">Władysław Strzemiński</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Sta%C5%BCewski" title="Henryk Stażewski">Henryk Stażewski</a> worked within the Constructivist idiom.</p>
<p>Distinguished contemporary artists include <a href="/wiki/Roman_Opa%C5%82ka" title="Roman Opałka">Roman Opałka</a>, Leon Tarasewicz, <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Nowosielski" title="Jerzy Nowosielski">Jerzy Nowosielski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wojciech_Siudmak" title="Wojciech Siudmak">Wojciech Siudmak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miros%C5%82aw_Ba%C5%82ka" title="Mirosław Bałka">Mirosław Bałka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Katarzyna_Kozyra" title="Katarzyna Kozyra">Katarzyna Kozyra</a> and Zbigniew Wąsiel in the younger generation. The most celebrated Polish sculptors include <a href="/wiki/Xawery_Dunikowski" title="Xawery Dunikowski">Xawery Dunikowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katarzyna_Kobro" title="Katarzyna Kobro">Katarzyna Kobro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alina_Szapocznikow" title="Alina Szapocznikow">Alina Szapocznikow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Abakanowicz" title="Magdalena Abakanowicz">Magdalena Abakanowicz</a>. Since the inter-war years, Polish art and documentary photography has enjoyed worldwide recognition. In the sixties the Polish Poster School was formed, with <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Tomaszewski_(poster_artist)" title="Henryk Tomaszewski (poster artist)">Henryk Tomaszewski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waldemar_%C5%9Awierzy" title="Waldemar Świerzy">Waldemar Świerzy</a> at its head.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA_200-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA-200">[200]</a></sup> Top fine Art schools in Poland are <a href="/wiki/Jan_Matejko_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" title="Jan Matejko Academy of Fine Arts">Jan Matejko Academy of Fine Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cracow_School_of_Art_and_Fashion_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracow School of Art and Fashion Design">Cracow School of Art and Fashion Design</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Fine_Arts_in_Warsaw" title="Academy of Fine Arts in Warsaw">Academy of Fine Arts in Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Academy_of_Szczecin" title="Art Academy of Szczecin">Art Academy of Szczecin</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Fine_Arts_in_Pozna%C5%84" title="University of Fine Arts in Poznań">University of Fine Arts in Poznań</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eugeniusz_Geppert_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" title="Eugeniusz Geppert Academy of Fine Arts">Eugeniusz Geppert Academy of Fine Arts</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Polish_architecture" title="Category:Polish architecture">Category:Polish architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg/170px-20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg/255px-20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg/340px-20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2761" data-file-height="4152" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20110917_Krakow_Kosciol_Mariacki_0306.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków">St. Mary's Basilica</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Main_Market_Square,_Krak%C3%B3w" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Market Square, Kraków">Main Market Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> is an example of <a href="/wiki/Brick_Gothic" title="Brick Gothic">Brick Gothic</a> architecture.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Polish cities and towns reflect a whole spectrum of European architectural styles. <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque architecture</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Church,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Andrew's Church, Kraków">St. Andrew's Church, Kraków</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Church,_Gda%C5%84sk" title="St. Mary's Church, Gdańsk">St. Mary's Church, Gdańsk</a>, is characteristic for the <a href="/wiki/Brick_Gothic" title="Brick Gothic">Brick Gothic</a> style found in Poland. Richly decorated <a href="/wiki/Attic_style" title="Attic style">attics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arcade_(architecture)" title="Arcade (architecture)">arcade</a> <a href="/wiki/Loggia" title="Loggia">loggias</a> are the common elements of the Polish Renaissance architecture,<sup id="cite_ref-szydlowiec_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szydlowiec-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RENAISSANCE_CULTURAL_BACKGROUND_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RENAISSANCE_CULTURAL_BACKGROUND-216">[216]</a></sup> as evident in the <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84_City_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Poznań City Hall">City Hall</a> in Poznań. For some time the late renaissance style known as <a href="/wiki/Mannerism" title="Mannerism">mannerism</a>, most notably in the <a href="/wiki/Cracow_Bishops%27_Palace_in_Kielce" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracow Bishops' Palace in Kielce">Bishop's Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kielce" title="Kielce">Kielce</a>, coexisted with the early baroque style, typified in the Church of Saints Peter and Paul in Kraków.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ayuntamiento,_Poznan,_Polonia,_2014-09-18,_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg/170px-Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg" width="170" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg/255px-Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg/340px-Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3088" data-file-height="5064" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ayuntamiento,_Poznan,_Polonia,_2014-09-18,_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ratusz" title="Ratusz">Ratusz</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Renaissance</a> City Hall in <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84" title="Poznań">Poznań</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>History has not been kind to Poland's architectural monuments. Nonetheless, a number of ancient structures has survived: castles, churches, and stately homes, often unique in the regional or European context. Some of them have been painstakingly restored, like <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Castle" title="Wawel Castle">Wawel Castle</a>, or completely reconstructed after being destroyed in the Second World War, including the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle_in_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Castle in Warsaw">Royal Castle</a> of Warsaw and the Old Town of <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>.</p>
<p>The architecture of Gdańsk is mostly of the Hanseatic variety, a Gothic style common among the former trading cities along the Baltic sea and in the northern part of Central Europe. The architectural style of <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a> is mainly representative of German architecture, since it was for centuries located within the German states. The centre of <a href="/wiki/Kazimierz_Dolny" title="Kazimierz Dolny">Kazimierz Dolny</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> is a good example of a well-preserved medieval town. Poland's ancient capital, <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, ranks among the best-preserved <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> and Renaissance urban complexes in Europe. Meanwhile, the legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Kresy" title="Kresy">Kresy</a> Marchlands of Poland's eastern regions, where Wilno and Lwów (now <i>Vilnius</i> and <i>Lviv</i>) were recognised as two major centres for the arts, played a special role in the development of Polish architecture, with Catholic church architecture deserving special note.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA_200-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second half of the 17th century is marked by <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> architecture. Side towers, such as those of <a href="/wiki/Branicki_Palace,_Bia%C5%82ystok" title="Branicki Palace, Białystok">Branicki Palace</a> in Białystok, are typical for the Polish baroque. The classical <a href="/wiki/Silesian_architecture" title="Silesian architecture">Silesian baroque</a> is represented by the University in Wrocław. The profuse decorations of the <a href="/wiki/Branicki_Palace,_Warsaw" title="Branicki Palace, Warsaw">Branicki Palace</a> in Warsaw are characteristic of the <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">rococo</a> style. The centre of Polish classicism was Warsaw under the rule of the last Polish king <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_August_Poniatowski" title="Stanisław August Poniatowski">Stanisław August Poniatowski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Palace" title="Łazienki Palace">Palace on the Water</a> is the most notable example of Polish <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical architecture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lublin_Castle" title="Lublin Castle">Lublin Castle</a> represents the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a> style in architecture, while the Izrael Poznański Palace in Łódź is an example of <a href="/wiki/Eclecticism" title="Eclecticism">eclecticism</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Polish_literature" title="Polish literature">Polish literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_philosophy_in_Poland" title="History of philosophy in Poland">History of philosophy in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG/140px-Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG" width="140" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG/210px-Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG/280px-Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG 2x" data-file-width="528" data-file-height="650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adam_Mickiewicz.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz" title="Adam Mickiewicz">Adam Mickiewicz</a> was an untiring promoter of Poland's culture and heritage during his many years in exile.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Polish_literature" title="Polish literature">Polish literature</a> dates back to the 12th century,<sup id="cite_ref-LIT01_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIT01-218">[218]</a></sup> and includes many renowned writers. Two Polish <a href="/wiki/Novelist" title="Novelist">novelists</a> have won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>: <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Sienkiewicz" title="Henryk Sienkiewicz">Henryk Sienkiewicz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Reymont" title="Władysław Reymont">Władysław Reymont</a>; along with two poets: <a href="/wiki/Czes%C5%82aw_Mi%C5%82osz" title="Czesław Miłosz">Czesław Miłosz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wis%C5%82awa_Szymborska" title="Wisława Szymborska">Wisława Szymborska</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_on_the_Nobel_Prize_in_Literature_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_on_the_Nobel_Prize_in_Literature-219">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Szymborska.27s_.27View.27:_Small_Truths_Sharply_Etched_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Szymborska.27s_.27View.27:_Small_Truths_Sharply_Etched-220">[220]</a></sup> A prose poet of the highest order, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Conrad" title="Joseph Conrad">Joseph Conrad</a> (1857–1924), son of the Polish dramatist <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Korzeniowski" title="Apollo Korzeniowski">Apollo Korzeniowski</a>, won worldwide fame with his English-language novels and stories that are informed with elements of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland" title="History of Poland">Polish national experience</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Among the best known <a href="/wiki/Romanticism_in_Poland" title="Romanticism in Poland">Polish Romantics</a> are the "<a href="/wiki/Three_Bards" title="Three Bards">Three Bards</a>" — the three <a href="/wiki/National_poets" class="mw-redirect" title="National poets">national poets</a> active in the age of partitions: <a href="/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz" title="Adam Mickiewicz">Adam Mickiewicz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki" title="Juliusz Słowacki">Juliusz Słowacki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zygmunt_Krasi%C5%84ski" title="Zygmunt Krasiński">Zygmunt Krasiński</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Blavascunas2008_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blavascunas2008-223">[223]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the Middle Ages, most Polish writers and scholars (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Jan_D%C5%82ugosz" title="Jan Długosz">Jan Długosz</a>) wrote only in Latin, the common language of European letters. This tradition was broken by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Kochanowski" title="Jan Kochanowski">Jan Kochanowski</a>, who became one of the first <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Polish Renaissance</a> authors to write most of his works in Polish, along with <a href="/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_Rej" title="Mikołaj Rej">Mikołaj Rej</a>. Also notable are the 19th and 20th-century Polish authors such as <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_Prus" title="Bolesław Prus">Bolesław Prus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kornel_Makuszy%C5%84ski" title="Kornel Makuszyński">Kornel Makuszyński</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Lem" title="Stanisław Lem">Stanisław Lem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Witold_Gombrowicz" title="Witold Gombrowicz">Witold Gombrowicz</a>, among others.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Poland" title="Television in Poland">Television in Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Poland" title="Media of Poland">Media of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Poland" title="Theatre of Poland">Theatre of Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Poland" title="Cinema of Poland">Cinema of Poland</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Video_gaming_in_Poland" title="Category:Video gaming in Poland">Category:Video gaming in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_(front).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_%28front%29.jpg/220px-Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_%28front%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_%28front%29.jpg/330px-Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_%28front%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_%28front%29.jpg/440px-Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_%28front%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_-_TVP_building_B_(front).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Headquarters of the national television network <a href="/wiki/Telewizja_Polska" title="Telewizja Polska">TVP</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland has instituted <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_press" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of press">freedom of press</a> since the fall of communism, a system under which the media was heavily politically controlled and censored. However, public TV and radio are still regulated by the government, this is exercised through an agency called <i><a href="/wiki/Krajowa_Rada_Radiofonii_i_Telewizji" title="Krajowa Rada Radiofonii i Telewizji">Krajowa Rada Radiofonii i Telewizji</a></i> (<i>The National Radio and Television Committee</i>), which is similar to television regulatory commissions in other developed nations.</p>
<p>Poland has a number of major media outlets, chief among which are the national television channels. <a href="/wiki/Telewizja_Polska" title="Telewizja Polska">TVP</a> is Poland's <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcasting</a> corporation; about a third of its income comes from a <a href="/wiki/Television_licence" title="Television licence">broadcast receiver licence</a>, while the rest is made through revenue from <a href="/wiki/Television_advertisement" title="Television advertisement">commercials</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sponsor_(commercial)" title="Sponsor (commercial)">sponsorships</a>. State television operates two mainstream channels, TVP 1 and TVP 2, as well as regional programs for each of the country's 16 <a href="/wiki/Voivodeship" title="Voivodeship">voivodeships</a>. In addition to these general channels, TVP runs a number of genre-specific programmes such as <a href="/wiki/TVP_Sport" title="TVP Sport">TVP Sport</a>, <a href="/wiki/TVP_Historia" title="TVP Historia">TVP Historia</a>, <a href="/wiki/TVP_Kultura" title="TVP Kultura">TVP Kultura</a>, <a href="/wiki/TVP_Seriale" title="TVP Seriale">TVP Seriale</a> and <a href="/wiki/TV_Polonia" class="mw-redirect" title="TV Polonia">TV Polonia</a>, the latter is a state-run channel dedicated to the transmission of Polish language television for the <a href="/wiki/Polish_diaspora" title="Polish diaspora">Polish diaspora</a> abroad.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_(8464360471).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_%288464360471%29.jpg/220px-Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_%288464360471%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_%288464360471%29.jpg/330px-Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_%288464360471%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_%288464360471%29.jpg/440px-Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_%288464360471%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Podczas_zawod%C3%B3w_IEM_(8464360471).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Intel_Extreme_Masters" title="Intel Extreme Masters">Intel Extreme Masters</a>, an <a href="/wiki/ESports" title="ESports">eSports</a> video game tournament in <a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Poland has several 24-hour news channels: <a href="/wiki/Polsat_News" title="Polsat News">Polsat News</a>, <a href="/wiki/TVP_Info" title="TVP Info">TVP Info</a> and <a href="/wiki/TVN_24" class="mw-redirect" title="TVN 24">TVN 24</a>. The two largest private television networks are <a href="/wiki/Polsat" title="Polsat">Polsat</a> and <a href="/wiki/TVN_(Poland)" title="TVN (Poland)">TVN</a>.</p>
<p>In Poland, daily newspapers like <i><a href="/wiki/Gazeta_Wyborcza" title="Gazeta Wyborcza">Gazeta Wyborcza</a></i> ("Electoral Gazette"), <i><a href="/wiki/Rzeczpospolita_(newspaper)" title="Rzeczpospolita (newspaper)">Rzeczpospolita</a></i> ("The Republic") and <i><a href="/wiki/Gazeta_Polska_Codziennie" title="Gazeta Polska Codziennie">Gazeta Polska Codziennie</a></i> ("Polish Daily Newspaper") provide traditional opinion and news, while tabloids such as <i><a href="/wiki/Fakt" title="Fakt">Fakt</a></i> provide more sensationalist journalism. <i>Rzeczpospolita</i>, founded in 1920 is one of the oldest newspapers still in operation. In 2006, it won a prestigious award for being, along with the <i><a href="/wiki/Guardian_(newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardian (newspaper)">Guardian</a></i> (a British daily), the best designed newspaper in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_wins_design_award_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_wins_design_award-224">[224]</a></sup> The most popular weeklies are <a href="/wiki/Tygodnik_Angora" title="Tygodnik Angora">Tygodnik Angora</a>, <a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/W_Sieci" class="extiw" title="pl:W Sieci">W Sieci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polityka" title="Polityka">Polityka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wprost" title="Wprost">Wprost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newsweek_Polska" title="Newsweek Polska">Newsweek Polska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Go%C5%9B%C4%87_Niedzielny" title="Gość Niedzielny">Gość Niedzielny</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gazeta_Polska" title="Gazeta Polska">Gazeta Polska</a>.</p>
<p>Poland also has emerged as a major hub for video game developers in Europe, with the country now being home to hundreds of studios. One of the most popular video game series developed in Poland includes <a href="/wiki/The_Witcher_(video_game)" title="The Witcher (video game)">The Witcher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a> hosts <a href="/wiki/Intel_Extreme_Masters" title="Intel Extreme Masters">Intel Extreme Masters</a>, one of the biggest <a href="/wiki/ESports" title="ESports">eSports</a> events in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Polish_cuisine" title="Polish cuisine">Polish cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg/220px-07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg/330px-07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg/440px-07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:07425_Jahrmarkt_in_Sanok_am_17_Juli_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Selection of hearty traditional comfort food from Poland including <a href="/wiki/Bigos" title="Bigos">bigos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage_roll" title="Cabbage roll">cabbage rolls</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%BBurek" class="mw-redirect" title="Żurek">żurek</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Pierogi" title="Pierogi">pierogi</a> and specialty breads</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Polish cuisine has evolved over the centuries to become very eclectic due to Poland's history. Polish cuisine shares many similarities with other <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European cuisines</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/German_cuisine" title="German cuisine">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_cuisine" title="Austrian cuisine">Austrian</a><sup id="cite_ref-Zibart_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zibart-227">[227]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Jewish_cuisine" title="Jewish cuisine">Jewish</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ashkenazic_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ashkenazic-228">[228]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_cuisine" title="Belarusian cuisine">Belarusian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_cuisine" title="Ukrainian cuisine">Ukrainian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_cuisine" title="Russian cuisine">Russian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Nigel_Roberts_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nigel_Roberts-229">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a> culinary traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Jerzy_Pasikowski_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jerzy_Pasikowski-230">[230]</a></sup> It is rich in meat, especially pork, chicken and beef (depending on the region) and winter vegetables (cabbage in the dish <i><a href="/wiki/Bigos" title="Bigos">bigos</a></i>), and spices.<sup id="cite_ref-polishmeals_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polishmeals-231">[231]</a></sup> It is also characteristic in its use of various kinds of <a href="/wiki/Noodle" title="Noodle">noodles</a> the most notable of which are <a href="/wiki/Kluski" title="Kluski">kluski</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereals</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kasha" title="Kasha">kasha</a></i> (from the Polish word <a href="/wiki/Kasza" class="mw-redirect" title="Kasza">kasza</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-websters_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-websters-232">[232]</a></sup> Polish cuisine is hearty and uses a lot of cream and eggs. Festive meals such as the meatless Christmas Eve dinner (<i><a href="/wiki/Wigilia" title="Wigilia">Wigilia</a></i>) or <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> breakfast could take days to prepare in their entirety.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Go%C5%82ka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Oscypek" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Go%C5%82ka.jpg/200px-Go%C5%82ka.jpg" width="200" height="123" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Go%C5%82ka.jpg/300px-Go%C5%82ka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Go%C5%82ka.jpg/400px-Go%C5%82ka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="790" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Oscypek" title="Oscypek">Oscypek</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Smoked_cheese" title="Smoked cheese">smoked cheese</a> made of salted sheep milk exclusively in the Polish <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">Tatra Mountains</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Bagel" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg/200px-Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg" width="200" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg/300px-Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg/400px-Bagel-Plain-Alt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2580" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Bagels" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagels">Bagels</a>, made from <a href="/wiki/Yeast" title="Yeast">yeasted</a> <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> dough, originated in Poland.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main course usually includes a serving of meat, such as roast, chicken, or <i><a href="/wiki/Kotlet_schabowy" title="Kotlet schabowy">kotlet schabowy</a></i> (breaded pork cutlet), vegetables, side dishes and salads, including <i>surówka</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[suˈrufka]</a></span> – shredded root vegetables with lemon and sugar (carrot, celeriac, <a href="/wiki/Searing" title="Searing">seared</a> beetroot) or sauerkraut (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <span lang="pl"><i>kapusta kiszona</i></span>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[kaˈpusta kʲiˈʂɔna]</a></span>). The side dishes are usually potatoes, rice or <i>kasza</i> (cereals). Meals conclude with a dessert such as <i><a href="/wiki/Cheesecake" title="Cheesecake">sernik</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Makowiec_(pastry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Makowiec (pastry)">makowiec</a></i> (a <a href="/wiki/Poppy_seed" title="Poppy seed">poppy seed</a> pastry), or <i>drożdżówka</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[drɔʐˈd͡ʐufka]</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Viennoiserie" title="Viennoiserie">yeast pastry</a>, and tea.</p>
<p>The Polish national dishes are <i><a href="/wiki/Bigos" title="Bigos">bigos</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈbiɡɔs]</a></span>; <i><a href="/wiki/Pierogi" title="Pierogi">pierogi</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[pʲɛˈrɔɡʲi]</a></span>; <i><a href="/wiki/Kielbasa" title="Kielbasa">kielbasa</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/Kotlet_schabowy" title="Kotlet schabowy">kotlet schabowy</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈkɔtlɛt sxaˈbɔvɨ]</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Breaded_cutlet" title="Breaded cutlet">breaded cutlet</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Go%C5%82%C4%85bki" title="Gołąbki">gołąbki</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ɡɔˈwɔ̃pkʲi]</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cabbage_roll" title="Cabbage roll">cabbage rolls</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Zrazy" title="Zrazy">zrazy</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈzrazɨ]</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Roulade" title="Roulade">roulade</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Roast" class="mw-redirect" title="Roast">pieczeń</a></i> roast <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈpʲɛt͡ʂɛɲ]</a></span>; sour <a href="/wiki/Cucumber_soup" title="Cucumber soup">cucumber soup</a> (<i>zupa ogórkowa</i>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈzupa ɔɡurˈkɔva]</a></span>); mushroom soup, (<i>zupa grzybowa</i>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈzupa ɡʐɨˈbɔva]</a></span> quite different from the North American <a href="/wiki/Cream_of_mushroom_soup" title="Cream of mushroom soup">cream of mushroom</a>); <i>zupa pomidorowa</i> <a href="/wiki/Tomato_soup" title="Tomato soup">tomato soup</a> <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈzupa pɔmidɔˈrɔva]</a></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-Marc_Heine_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marc_Heine-234">[234]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Ros%C3%B3%C5%82" title="Rosół">rosół</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈrɔɕuw]</a></span> variety of meat broth; <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%BBurek" class="mw-redirect" title="Żurek">żurek</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈʐurɛk]</a></span> sour rye soup; <i><a href="/wiki/Flaki" class="mw-redirect" title="Flaki">flaki</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈflakʲi]</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tripe_soup" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripe soup">tripe soup</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Barszcz" class="mw-redirect" title="Barszcz">barszcz</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[barʂt͡ʂ]</a></span> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%82odnik" class="mw-redirect" title="Chłodnik">chłodnik</a></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈxwɔdɲik]</a></span> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_Strybel_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Strybel-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traditional alcoholic beverages include honey <a href="/wiki/Mead" title="Mead">mead</a>, widespread since the 13th century, beer, wine and vodka (old Polish names include <i>okowita</i> and <i>gorzałka</i>). The world's first written mention of vodka originates from Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-KRPS_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KRPS-236">[236]</a></sup> The most popular alcoholic drinks at present are beer and wine which took over from vodka more popular in the years 1980–98.<sup id="cite_ref-beverages_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beverages-237">[237]</a></sup> Tea remains common in Polish society since the 19th century, whilst coffee is drunk widely since the 18th century. Other frequently consumed beverages include various mineral waters and juices, soft drinks popularized by the fast-food chains since the late 20th century, as well as <a href="/wiki/Buttermilk" title="Buttermilk">buttermilk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soured_milk" title="Soured milk">soured milk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kefir" title="Kefir">kefir</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Poland" title="Sport in Poland">Sport in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:287px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg/285px-Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg" width="285" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg/428px-Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg/570px-Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="1800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_Narodowy_w_Warszawie_20120422.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Warsaw" title="National Stadium, Warsaw">National Stadium</a> in Warsaw, home of <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">national football team</a>, and one of the host stadiums of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> are among the country's most popular sports, with a rich history of international competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-FIFA_World_Cup_Statistics-Poland_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA_World_Cup_Statistics-Poland-238">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FIFA_Statistics_.E2.80.93_Poland_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA_Statistics_.E2.80.93_Poland-239">[239]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Track and field athletics">Track and field</a>, basketball, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, boxing, <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts" title="Mixed martial arts">MMA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">motorcycle speedway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ski_jumping" title="Ski jumping">ski jumping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">cross-country skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, tennis, fencing, swimming and <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a> are other popular sports.</p>
<p>The golden era of <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Poland" title="Football in Poland">football in Poland</a> occurred throughout the 1970s and went on until the early 1980s when the <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Polish national football team</a> achieved their best results in any FIFA World Cup competitions finishing 3rd place in <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">the 1974</a> and <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">the 1982</a> tournaments. The team won a gold medal <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the Summer Olympics">in football</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a> and two silver medals, <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">in 1976</a> and <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">in 1992</a>. Poland, along with Ukraine, hosted the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA European Football Championship in 2012</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-warsaw-life_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warsaw-life-240">[240]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Derby_Pomorza_2009_(Bydgoszcz)2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Derby_Pomorza_2009_%28Bydgoszcz%292.jpg/220px-Derby_Pomorza_2009_%28Bydgoszcz%292.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Derby_Pomorza_2009_%28Bydgoszcz%292.jpg/330px-Derby_Pomorza_2009_%28Bydgoszcz%292.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Derby_Pomorza_2009_%28Bydgoszcz%292.jpg/440px-Derby_Pomorza_2009_%28Bydgoszcz%292.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Derby_Pomorza_2009_(Bydgoszcz)2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">Motorcycle speedway</a> <i>(Żużel)</i> race in the <a href="/wiki/Ekstraliga_(speedway)" title="Ekstraliga (speedway)">Speedway Ekstraliga</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Poland_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Poland men's national volleyball team">Polish men's national volleyball team</a> is ranked <a href="/wiki/FIVB_World_Rankings" title="FIVB World Rankings">as 3rd</a> in the world. Volleyball team won a gold medal in <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Volleyball at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament">Olympic 1976 Montreal</a> and two gold medals in <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship">FIVB World Championship</a> <a href="/wiki/1974_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship" title="1974 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship">1974</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship" title="2014 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship">2014</a> and hosted.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mariusz_Pudzianowski" title="Mariusz Pudzianowski">Mariusz Pudzianowski</a> is a highly successful strongman competitor and has won more <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Strongest_Man" title="World's Strongest Man">World's Strongest Man</a> titles than any other competitor in the world, winning the event in 2008 for the fifth time. The first Polish <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> driver, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kubica" title="Robert Kubica">Robert Kubica</a>, has brought awareness of Formula One racing to Poland. He won the <a href="/wiki/2008_Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="2008 Canadian Grand Prix">2008 Canadian Grand Prix</a> and now does <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">rallying</a> following a crash in 2011 that left him unable to drive F1 cars.</p>
<p>Poland has made a distinctive mark <a href="/wiki/Speedway_in_Poland" title="Speedway in Poland">in motorcycle speedway racing</a> thanks to <a href="/wiki/Tomasz_Gollob" title="Tomasz Gollob">Tomasz Gollob</a>, a highly successful Polish rider. The top <a href="/wiki/Speedway_Ekstraliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Speedway Ekstraliga">Ekstraliga</a> division has one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_attendance_figures_at_domestic_professional_sports_leagues#Outdoor" title="List of attendance figures at domestic professional sports leagues">the highest average attendances</a> for any sport in Poland. The <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_speedway_team" title="Poland national speedway team">national speedway team of Poland</a>, one of the major teams in international speedway,<sup id="cite_ref-Speedway_World_Cup:_Poland_win_2010_Speedway_World_Cup_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Speedway_World_Cup:_Poland_win_2010_Speedway_World_Cup-242">[242]</a></sup> has won the <a href="/wiki/Speedway_World_Team_Cup" title="Speedway World Team Cup">Speedway World Team Cup</a> championships three times consecutively, in 2009, 2010, and 2011. No team has ever managed such feat.<sup id="cite_ref-polishforums_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polishforums-243">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup></p>
<p>Poles made significant achievements in mountaineering, in particular, in the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> and the winter ascending of the <a href="/wiki/Eight-thousander" title="Eight-thousander">eight-thousanders</a>. The most famous Polish climbers are <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Kukuczka" title="Jerzy Kukuczka">Jerzy Kukuczka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Wielicki" title="Krzysztof Wielicki">Krzysztof Wielicki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piotr_Pustelnik" title="Piotr Pustelnik">Piotr Pustelnik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Zawada" title="Andrzej Zawada">Andrzej Zawada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maciej_Berbeka" title="Maciej Berbeka">Maciej Berbeka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artur_Hajzer" title="Artur Hajzer">Artur Hajzer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Czok" title="Andrzej Czok">Andrzej Czok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wojciech_Kurtyka" title="Wojciech Kurtyka">Wojciech Kurtyka</a>, and women <a href="/wiki/Wanda_Rutkiewicz" title="Wanda Rutkiewicz">Wanda Rutkiewicz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kinga_Baranowska" title="Kinga Baranowska">Kinga Baranowska</a>. Polish mountains are one of the tourist attractions of the country. Hiking, climbing, skiing and mountain biking and attract numerous tourists every year from all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-turism_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turism-149">[149]</a></sup> Water sports are the most popular summer recreation activities, with ample locations for fishing, canoeing, kayaking, sailing and windsurfing especially in the northern regions of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<dl>
<dd>a. <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_anone"><a href="#ref_anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> In other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Poland" title="Languages of Poland">languages of Poland</a>:</dd>
<dd>*<a href="/wiki/Kashubian_language" title="Kashubian language">Kashubian</a>: <span lang="csb"><i>Repùblika Pòlskô</i></span></dd>
<dd>*<a href="/wiki/Silesian_language" title="Silesian language">Silesian</a>: <span lang="szl"><i>Polsko Republik</i></span></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>b. <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bnone"><a href="#ref_bnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Numerous sources state that Polish Army was the Allies' fourth biggest fighting contingent. <a href="/wiki/Steven_J._Zaloga" class="mw-redirect" title="Steven J. Zaloga">Steven J. Zaloga</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richard_Hook&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Richard Hook (page does not exist)">Richard Hook</a> write that "by the war's end the Polish Army was the fourth largest contingent of the Allied coalition after the armed forces of the Soviet Union, the United States and the United Kingdom".<sup id="cite_ref-ZalogaHook1982_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZalogaHook1982-250">[250]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Jan_Lerski" title="Jerzy Jan Lerski">Jerzy Jan Lerski</a> writes "All in all, the Polish units, although divided and controlled by different political orientation, constituted the fourth largest Allied force, after the America, British and Soviet Armies."<sup id="cite_ref-Lerski1996_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lerski1996-251">[251]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/M._K._Dziewanowski" class="mw-redirect" title="M. K. Dziewanowski">M. K. Dziewanowski</a> has noted that "if Polish forces fighting in the east and west were added to the resistance fighters, Poland had the fourth largest Allied army in the war (after the USSR, the U.S. and Britain)".<sup id="cite_ref-Walters1988_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walters1988-252">[252]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>The claim of the fourth biggest Ally needs to be reconsidered, however. Throughout the war, Poland's position varied from the 2nd biggest Ally (after the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of France">fall of France</a>, when Polish army outnumbered the French) to perhaps the 5th at the end of it (after the US, Soviet Union, China and Britain). Please see the analysis in <a href="/wiki/Polish_contribution_to_World_War_II" title="Polish contribution to World War II">Polish contribution to World War II</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>c. <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cnone"><a href="#ref_cnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Sources vary with regards to what was the largest resistance movement during World War II. The confusion often stems from the fact that as war progressed, some resistance movements grew larger – and other diminished. Polish territories were mostly freed from Nazi German control in the years 1944–45, eliminating the need for their respective (anti-Nazi) partisan forces in Poland (although the <a href="/wiki/Cursed_soldiers" title="Cursed soldiers">cursed soldiers</a> continued to fight against the Soviets). Several sources note that Polish <a href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" class="mw-redirect" title="Armia Krajowa">Armia Krajowa</a> was the largest resistance movement in Nazi-occupied Europe. <a href="/wiki/Norman_Davies" title="Norman Davies">Norman Davies</a> wrote: "Armia Krajowa (Home Army), the AK, which could fairly claim to be the largest of European resistance";<sup id="cite_ref-google12_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google12-253">[253]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregor_Dallas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gregor Dallas (page does not exist)">Gregor Dallas</a> wrote "Home Army (Armia Krajowa or AK) in late 1943 numbered around 400000, making it the largest resistance organization in Europe";<sup id="cite_ref-google13_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google13-254">[254]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mark_Wyman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mark Wyman (page does not exist)">Mark Wyman</a> wrote "Armia Krajowa was considered the largest underground resistance unit in wartime Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-google14_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google14-255">[255]</a></sup> Certainly, Polish resistance was the largest resistance till German <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Yugoslavia" title="Invasion of Yugoslavia">invasion of Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of the Soviet Union">invasion of the Soviet Union</a> in 1941. After that point, the numbers of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_partisans" title="Soviet partisans">Soviet partisans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_partisans" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav partisans">Yugoslav partisans</a> begun growing rapidly. The numbers of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_partisans" title="Soviet partisans">Soviet partisans</a> quickly caught up and were very similar to that of the Polish resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-historiographical_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historiographical-256">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vuk.C5.A1i.C4.872003_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vuk.C5.A1i.C4.872003-257">[257]</a></sup> The numbers of Tito's <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_partisans" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav partisans">Yugoslav partisans</a> were roughly similar to those of the Polish and Soviet partisans in the first years of the war (1941–42), but grew rapidly in the latter years, outnumbering the Polish and Soviet partisans by 2:1 or more (estimates give Yugoslavian forces about 800,000 in 1945, to Polish and Soviet forces of 400,000 in 1944).<sup id="cite_ref-Vuk.C5.A1i.C4.872003_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vuk.C5.A1i.C4.872003-257">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ac_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ac-258">[258]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
</div>
